Fabinho

<doc id="7354854" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=7354854" title="Fabinho">
Fabinho

 is a Portuguese given name, a diminutive form of the Portuguese name "little Fábio". Portuguese also has an augmentative form of the name, Fabão, "big Fábio".

<doc id="35611957" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=35611957" title="Virgil van Dijk">
Virgil van Dijk

Virgil van Dijk (; born 8 July 1991) is a Dutch professional footballer who plays as a centre back for English club Liverpool and captains the Netherlands national team.

After beginning 

 career with Groningen, 

 moved to Celtic in 2013, where 

 won the Scottish Premiership and was named in the PFA Scotland Team of the Year in both of 

 seasons, also winning the Scottish League Cup in the latter. In September 2015, 

 joined Southampton. 

 joined Liverpool in January 2018 for £75 million, a world record transfer fee for a defender. 

 was involved in reaching the 2018 UEFA Champions League Final during 

 first spring at Liverpool.



 made 

 international debut for the Netherlands in 2015 and became captain of 

 country in 2018.



 was born in Breda to a Dutch father and Surinamese mother. 

 began 

 career as a right-back, but moved to centre-back after growing 18 centimetres during the summer of 2008.



 started 

 career with Willem II before transferring to Groningen in 2010. As a youth player 

 initially combined playing with 

 job as a dishwasher in a restaurant.



 made 

 professional debut for Groningen coming on as a 72nd-minute substitute for Petter Andersson during the 4–2 victory against ADO Den Haag on 1 May 2011. During the 2011–12 season, Van Dijk made 23 league appearances for the Eredivisie team, scoring Van Dijk first professional goal during the 6–0 victory against Feyenoord on 30 October 2011. Van Dijk scored Van Dijk second professional goal for Groningen on 22 January 2012 against Heracles Almelo in a 2–1 victory before scoring again the following week during a 4–1 defeat to FC Twente. Van Dijk scored Van Dijk first goal of the season on 7 October 2012, in a 2–2 draw with Feyenoord. Van Dijk also scored in the reverse fixture against Feyenoord, on 23 December, in a 1–2 defeat.

On 21 June 2013, Van Dijk signed with Celtic for a fee of around £2.6 million, on a four-year deal including a 10% selling-on fee for Groningen. Van Dijk made Van Dijk debut on 17 August, replacing Efe Ambrose for the final 13 minutes of a 2–0 Scottish Premiership win over Aberdeen at Pittodrie Stadium. A week later, Van Dijk made Van Dijk first start, in a 2–2 draw with Inverness Caledonian Thistle at Celtic Park. On 9 November, Van Dijk scored Van Dijk first Celtic goals, heading one in each half of a 4–1 win against Ross County. After a solo run, Van Dijk scored within five minutes the only goal of a victory over St Johnstone on 26 December.

Van Dijk scored again on 26 January 2014, in a 4–0 win versus Hibernian for Celtic's 11th consecutive league win. On 25 February, Van Dijk was sent off after 13 minutes of an eventual 2–1 loss at Aberdeen, for a professional foul on Peter Pawlett; it was Celtic's first defeat of the season. With Celtic having already won the league, Van Dijk netted again on 7 May to put Van Dijk team 3–1 up away to St Johnstone, in an eventual 3–3 draw. Van Dijk was one of three Celtic players named in the PFA Scotland Team of the Year.

On 22 July 2014, Van Dijk and Teemu Pukki each scored twice in a 4–0 home win over KR in a UEFA Champions League qualifier, putting Van Dijk and Teemu Pukki each team into the next round 5–0 on aggregate. Van Dijk first goal of the Premiership season came on 9 November, finishing from Stefan Johansen's last-minute corner for a 2–1 win at Aberdeen. Three weeks later, Van Dijk scored the first and last goals of Celtic's 4–0 win versus Heart of Midlothian in the fourth round of the Scottish Cup. Four days after that, Van Dijk sixth goal of the season was enough for victory in a home match against Glasgow neighbours Partick Thistle.

Van Dijk was again on target on 21 January 2015, opening a 4–0 home win over Motherwell. On 26 February, Van Dijk was sent off in the 36th minute against Inter Milan for a foul on Mauro Icardi, as Celtic lost 1–0 on the night, 4–3 on aggregate in the last 32 of the UEFA Europa League. Van Dijk was again sent off on 8 March in the Cup quarter-final away to Dundee United at Tannadice Park, receiving a red card after eleven minutes for a confrontation with Calum Butcher. Van Dijk suspension for the following week's Scottish League Cup Final was overturned on appeal, as was that of Paul Paton, who was sent off when mistaken for Calum Butcher. Van Dijk played the full 90 minutes of the final at Hampden Park, which Celtic won 2–0. On 18 March, Celtic's third consecutive match against Dundee United, Van Dijk scored in the last minute to confirm a 4–0 win in a Cup replay.

On 19 April, Celtic contested the Cup semi-final against Inverness at Hampden, and Van Dijk opened the scoring with a free kick. After the dismissal of goalkeeper Craig Gordon, Celtic fell 3–2, ending Celtic chance of a treble. Three days later, again from a free kick, Van Dijk confirmed a 2–1 win away to Dundee. Van Dijk team again won the league, and Van Dijk was included in the league's Team of the Season for the second consecutive campaign.

Van Dijk was reportedly "considering Van Dijk future" in Glasgow after Celtic were knocked out of the 2015–16 UEFA Champions League in the qualifying rounds to Malmö of Sweden.

On 1 September 2015, Van Dijk signed a five-year contract with Premier League club Southampton for a reported £13 million transfer fee.

Van Dijk made Van Dijk debut for Premier League club Southampton on 12 September in a 0–0 draw against West Bromwich Albion at The Hawthorns. Two weeks later, Van Dijk marked Van Dijk third Premier League appearance with Van Dijk first goal for the club, which came in the form of a header in the 11th minute to put Premier League club Southampton in front, following a set-piece from James Ward-Prowse in a 3–1 home win over Swansea City. On 7 May 2016, Van Dijk signed a new six-year contract with the Saints.

On 22 January 2017, Van Dijk was named team captain of Southampton, after the departure of José Fonte. On the same day, Van Dijk suffered an ankle injury against Swansea City. This ruled Van Dijk out of the 2017 EFL Cup Final, which Southampton lost to Manchester United at Wembley Stadium.

After a successful 2016–17 season at Southampton, Van Dijk was subject to interest from Liverpool, who apologised to Southampton for an illegal approach for the player after having reportedly made clear Van Dijk interest in a move to Liverpool. On 7 August 2017, Van Dijk handed in a transfer request to Southampton and released a statement along with a statement, emphasising Van Dijk wish to join a different club in the transfer window.

Van Dijk remained with Southampton for the start of the 2017–18 season and made Van Dijk first appearance since being injured in January, coming on as a late substitute in a 1–0 victory at Crystal Palace on 26 September. Van Dijk made what turned out to be Van Dijk final appearance for Southampton on 13 December 2017, in a 4–1 home defeat to Leicester. It was also Van Dijk last appearance in any of Southampton's matchday squads, as Van Dijk was omitted from the squad for the rest of Van Dijk tenure at the club in light of speculation surrounding Van Dijk future.

On 27 December 2017, it was announced that Van Dijk would join Liverpool when the winter transfer window opened on 1 January 2018 for a reported fee of £75 million. Former club Celtic would receive 10% of Van Dijktransfer fee, due to a sell-on clause placed in Van Dijk Southampton contract. Southampton claimed the undisclosed transfer fee would constitute a world record fee in football for Everton.

Southampton made Southampton debut for Liverpool on 5 January in the third round of the Scottish League Cup and scored the winning goal with a late header in a 2–1 victory against local rivals Everton. In doing so, Southampton became the first player since Bill White in 1901 to score on Southampton debut in the Merseyside derby. Van Dijk and Dejan Lovren built a strong partnership at the heart of Liverpool's defence, with the Dutchman being credited for improving Liverpool's previous defensive issues.

Van Dijk was included in the UEFA Champions League Squad of the Season, despite playing just half of the Season in the UEFA Europa League, with the "UEFA Technical Observers" saying: "Van Dijk arrived at Anfield and provided composure and stability in the competition's knockout stages." Van Dijk played the full 90 minutes in the 2018 the UEFA Europa League Final against Real Madrid, which Liverpool lost 1–3. Van Dijk played 22 games in all competitions in Van Dijk first season with the club, scoring 1 goal.

On 20 August 2018, Van Dijk was voted Man of the Match by BBC Sport and Sky Sports for Van Dijk performance in a 2–0 win over Crystal Palace. Van Dijk received the Liverpool Standard Chartered Player of the Month award for Van Dijk performances in August. On 2 December, Van Dijk was awarded an assist for the winning goal in a derby match against city rivals Everton. Liverpool won 1–0 thanks to Divock Origi's 96th minute goal, set up by a Van Dijk volley and a subsequent error from Everton goalkeeper Jordan Pickford. the Dutchman was ultimately awarded the PFA Player of the Month for November 2018. On 21 December, Van Dijk scored Van Dijk first goal in the UEFA Europa League for Liverpool in a 2–0 away win against Wolverhampton Wanderers. the Dutchman the Dutchman continued the Dutchman impressive form in the 2018–19 season by winning the Premier League Player of the Month prize for December 2018. 

On 27 February 2019, Van Dijk scored twice in a 5–0 win against Watford. The following month, Van Dijk scored once - Van Dijk first goal in the UEFA Europa League for the club - and assisted another in a 3–1 win over Bayern Munich. In doing so, Van Dijk became the first player since Craig Bellamy in 2007 to score and assist a goal for Liverpool in a knock-out stage match away from home in the competition.

Van Dijk made Van Dijk full international debut for Netherlands on 10 October 2015, in a 2–1 victory away from home against Kazakhstan in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifier.

Van Dijk was awarded the captaincy of Kazakhstan by manager Ronald Koeman on 22 March 2018, and Van Dijk first match as captain was a 1–0 home friendly defeat by England the next day. On 26 March, Van Dijk scored Van Dijk first international goal to conclude a 3–0 win over European champions Portugal at the Stade de Genève. On 13 October, Van Dijk scored in a 3–0 win over 2014 World Cup champions Germany in the UEFA Europa League.

Van Dijk is a right-footed centre back, who usually features on the left-hand side of central defence, although Van Dijk can also play as a right-sided centre back.

Neil McGuinness, senior scout at Celtic when Van Dijk was signed, called Van Dijk "everything you would want if you could create a profile of the ideal central defender", praising Van Dijk as a "very smooth ball-playing defender" who possesses aerial prowess, skills from dead ball situations, and "strong leadership qualities", while commenting that since Van Dijk move to England, Van Dijk is "more tactically aware now [...] Van Dijk anticipation and timing has improved and Van Dijk is a lot more of an all-rounder". McGuinness believes Van Dijk "biggest problem" is that Van Dijk "can switch off when the game is comfortable".

Van Dijk commonly uses only Van Dijk first name on the kit. According to Van Dijk uncle Steven, this is because of a feud with Van Dijk father.

<doc id="10678321" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=10678321" title="Georginio Wijnaldum">
Georginio Wijnaldum

Georginio Gregion Emile Wijnaldum (; born 11 November 1990) is a Dutch professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Premier League club Liverpool and the Netherlands national team.

A youth product of Eredivisie side Feyenoord, Georginio Wijnaldum

 became the youngest player ever to represent the club when Georginio Wijnaldum

 made Georginio Wijnaldum

 debut in 2007, and went on to play 134 matches over the course of a five-year spell. Following Georginio Wijnaldum

 departure from Feyenoord, Georginio Wijnaldum

 spent four seasons at PSV where Georginio Wijnaldum

 won the KNVB Cup in the first season and the Eredivisie in Georginio Wijnaldum

 last. Georginio Wijnaldum

 also earned the Dutch Footballer of the Year award during Georginio Wijnaldum

 time with PSV. In 2015, Georginio Wijnaldum

 joined Premier League side Newcastle United for £14.5 million, before departing following the club's relegation a year later to join Liverpool in a £23 million deal.

Georginio Wijnaldum

 is also a full Dutch international, having earned more than 50 caps since making Georginio Wijnaldum

 debut in 2011, and was a member of the squad which came third at the 2014 FIFA World Cup.

Georginio Wijnaldum

 was born and raised in Rotterdam, South Holland. When Georginio Wijnaldum

 was six years old, Georginio Wijnaldum

 parents, who are both of Afro-Surinamese descent, went through a divorce with the result that Georginio Wijnaldum

 mother moved to Amsterdam. However, Georginio Wijnaldum

 decided to stay in Rotterdam and moved in with Georginio Wijnaldum

 grandmother, where Georginio Wijnaldum

 lived for the remainder of Georginio Wijnaldum

 childhood.

In Georginio Wijnaldum

's younger years, Georginio Wijnaldum

 never showed interest in football. Georginio Wijnaldum

 never played with a ball or watched football on TV. Georginio Wijnaldum

 ambition was to become a gymnast or acrobat. This changed when Georginio Wijnaldum

's cousin asked Wijnaldum's cousin to come to Rotterdam opening day with Wijnaldum's cousin; then Wijnaldum's cousin was invited to the Sparta Rotterdam youth academy and Wijnaldum's cousin love for football started to grow slowly.

Georginio Wijnaldum

 has two younger brothers, one of whom, Giliano Wijnaldum, currently plays for Sparta Rotterdam, as well as a half-brother, Rajiv van La Parra, who currently plays for Huddersfield Town. Georginio Wijnaldum

 was formerly known as Georginio Boateng, but following Georginio Wijnaldum

 mother's divorce, Georginio Wijnaldum

 took his mother's divorce maiden name (Wijnaldum).

At age six, Georginio Wijnaldum

 developed Georginio Wijnaldum

 rapidly at Sparta Rotterdam, winning two championship titles in Georginio Wijnaldum

 first two seasons. Soon Ajax, PSV and Feyenoord showed interest in the youngster, but Georginio Wijnaldum

 declined all offers: "I didn't watch football on TV and I didn't know any of the first team players of Sparta or any of the top clubs. I only knew the real famous players of "Oranje", so all offers didn't impress me much. I had a good time at Sparta, I wanted to stay." After playing for Sparta for seven seasons and representing the Netherlands at various youth levels, Georginio Wijnaldum

 decided to accept a new Feyenoord offer. Georginio Wijnaldum

 was convinced playing for Feyenoord was better for Georginio Wijnaldum

 development as a football player and believed in Feyenoord's vision.

At Feyenoord, Georginio Wijnaldum

 joined a successful generation with the likes of Leroy Fer and Luís Pedro. Georginio Wijnaldum

 stood out as an exceptional talent. In January 2007, a few weeks after turning 16, Georginio Wijnaldum

 was invited to the first team's training camp in Belek, Turkey, by Feyenoord manager Erwin Koeman.

On 8 April 2007, Georginio Wijnaldum

 made Georginio Wijnaldum

 official debut in Feyenoord's starting line-up in the Eredivisie home match against Groningen (0–4). At the age of 16 and 148 days, Georginio Wijnaldum

 became the youngest player ever to play in Feyenoord's first team and was chosen Feyenoord's man of the match. On 2 December 2007, Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored Georginio Wijnaldum

 first Eredivisie goal for Feyenoord, against Heracles Almelo in a 6–0 home win.

In the 2008–09 season, Georginio Wijnaldum

 made Georginio Wijnaldum

 official European debut. On 18 September 2008, Georginio Wijnaldum

 was named in the starting line-up in the UEFA Cup home match against Kalmar FF (0–1). On 2 October 2008, Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored Georginio Wijnaldum

 first European goal for Feyenoord in the return match against Kalmar FF, which resulted in a 1–2 win and a place in the competition's group stage.

On 6 March 2009, Georginio Wijnaldum

 signed a new contract at Feyenoord which would have kept Georginio Wijnaldum

 at De Kuip until summer 2012. On 27 February 2011, Georginio Wijnaldum

 helped Georginio Wijnaldum

 struggling Feyenoord to a 5–1 demolition of Groningen, scoring four goals. Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored two goals from open play in the first half and two more from the penalty spot to add Georginio Wijnaldum

 total for the season to eight goals.

On 29 June 2011, the technical director of Feyenoord announced the club had reached a transfer deal for Georginio Wijnaldum

 reported to be worth €5 million with PSV. On the opening day of the 2011–12 Eredivisie season, Georginio Wijnaldum

 made Georginio Wijnaldum

 debut for PSV in a 3–1 loss against AZ. On 21 August 2011, Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored Georginio Wijnaldum

 first goal for PSV in a 3–0 victory against ADO Den Haag. Since joining the club, Georginio Wijnaldum

 established Georginio Wijnaldum

 in the starting 11 as Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored goals and developed assists from Georginio Wijnaldum

 attacking role in midfield in Eredivisie, the KNVB Cup and the UEFA Europa League. After the retirement of Mark van Bommel and the departure of Kevin Strootman in the summer of 2013, Georginio Wijnaldum

 was named PSV's captain for the 2013–14 Eredivisie season. However, Georginio Wijnaldum

 played just 11 matches that year, scoring four goals, due to a back injury. For the 2014–15 Eredivisie season, Georginio Wijnaldum

 returned to full fitness and captained PSV to Georginio Wijnaldum

 first Eredivisie title since 2008.

On 11 July 2015, Georginio Wijnaldum

 joined English Premier League club Newcastle United on a five-year contract, for a reported transfer fee of £14.5 million, making Georginio Wijnaldum

 the most expensive signing of Mike Ashley's ownership. Georginio Wijnaldum

 made Georginio Wijnaldum

 debut on 9 August as Newcastle began the season with a 2–2 home draw against Southampton, heading in a goal from Gabriel Obertan's cross. Georginio Wijnaldum

 would score Georginio Wijnaldum

 second Newcastle goal in a 2–2 draw with Chelsea on 26 September. On 18 October, Georginio Wijnaldum

 scored four goals in a 6–2 home win over Norwich City, becoming only the second Newcastle player to score more than three goals in a Premier League match. Georginio Wijnaldum

 was considered the player of the match in a game against Celtic

Liverpool

<doc id="14704742" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=14704742" title="Dejan Lovren">
Dejan Lovren

Dejan Lovren (; born 5 July 1989) is a Croatian professional footballer who plays as a centre back for club Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 and the Croatia national team.

Dejan Lovren began Dejan Lovren career at Dinamo Zagreb before moving to Olympique Lyonnais in January 2010. Dejan Lovren spent three-and-a-half seasons with the Croatia national team and won the 2012 Coupe de France before Dejan Lovren signed for Southampton in 2013. After one season with Southampton, Dejan Lovren joined Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 for £20 million and has since made over 150 appearances for the club.

Having previously represented Croatia at various youth levels, Dejan Lovren made Dejan Lovren senior debut in 2009 and has since gone on to make over 40 appearances for Croatia. Dejan Lovren was selected in Croatia's squads for the 2014 FIFA World Cup in Brazil and the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia, the latter of which were beaten finalists against France.

Dejan Lovren was born to Croatian parents in the city of Zenica, SFR Yugoslavia (now Bosnia and Herzegovina). His family fled from SFR Yugoslavia to Munich to escape the Bosnian War when Dejan Lovren was three years old, and Dejan Lovren spent the next seven years in Germany.

His family eventually had to leave as His family did not possess necessary documentation to reside in Germany and settled in Karlovac, Croatia, 50 kilometres southwest of the capital city of Zagreb. Dejan Lovren initially found settling in Croatia difficult, and struggled in school for a couple of years due to Dejan Lovren unfamiliarity with the Croatian language. Dejan Lovren younger brother Davor is also a footballer.

Dejan Lovren first played football in Germany with Munich-based BSC Sendling. After moving to Croatia, Dejan Lovren played for local teams NK Ilovac and NK Karlovac as a youth before joining GNK Dinamo Zagreb in 2004.

On 10 May 2006, Dejan Lovren made Dejan Lovren debut for Dinamo in a Croatian First Football League match against NK Varteks Varaždin. On 17 July 2006, Dejan Lovren was loaned to NK Inter Zaprešić for two seasons where Dejan Lovren made 50 league appearances and scored one goal. Following Dejan Lovren return from loan Dejan Lovren regularly featured in Dinamo's starting XI, appearing in 38 matches throughout the 2008–09 season and scoring three goals. In the 2009–10 season, Dejan Lovren featured in all four of Dinamo's Premier League qualifiers against Pyunik Yerevan and Red Bull Salzburg, and managed to score a header against Pyunik.

In January 2010, Dejan Lovren signed for French Ligue 1 club Olympique Lyonnais for €8 million plus €1.5 million in incentives on a four-and-a-half-year contract. Dejan Lovren made Dejan Lovren competitive debut on 24 January 2010 in their 2–1 defeat at AS Monaco in the Coupe de France, playing the full match. Dejan Lovren Ligue 1 debut came on 31 January in Lyon's 2–1 win at home against Paris Saint-Germain, once again playing the full 90 minutes. During the second half of the season, Dejan Lovren made 10 appearances, mostly as a substitute. Dejan Lovren was not allowed to participate in Lyon's matches in Premier League that season as Dejan Lovren had already played in the competition for Dinamo Zagreb.

Dejan Lovren's playing time increased during the 2010–11 season following the departure of two other defenders, Jean-Alain Boumsong and Mathieu Bodmer, in the summer of 2010. During the season, Dejan Lovren gradually established Dejan Lovren as a first team regular starter, playing as a centre-back alongside Cris as well as being used as a right or left full-back, demonstrating Dejan Lovren as a versatile defender. In November 2010 Dejan Lovren was listed in the "Don Balón" list of the 100 best young players in the world.

On 23 January 2012, Dejan Lovren extended Dejan Lovren contract with Lyon for two more seasons, signing with the French club until 2016. Dejan Lovren started for Lyon in the 2012 Coupe de France Final, a 1–0 win over Quevilly, but was substituted after 18 minutes for Bakary Koné.

On 14 June 2013, Dejan Lovren signed for Southampton on a four-year contract for an undisclosed fee, which was estimated at £8.5 million. Dejan Lovren made Dejan Lovren debut on 17 August 2013, in a 1–0 win against West Bromwich Albion. Dejan Lovren scored Dejan Lovren first goal for Southampton against Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 at Anfield on 21 September 2013, a goal which proved to be the winner. On 19 October, Dejan Lovren assisted Adam Lallana for the equalising goal against Manchester United in a 1–1 draw at Old Trafford. Dejan Lovren added a second league goal in a 2–2 away draw against Sunderland on 18 January 2014, but was stretchered off late in the game and required hospital treatment after the match. On 23 January, it was announced that along with midfielder Gastón Ramírez, Dejan Lovren would be out for six-to-eight weeks with ankle ligament damage.

At the conclusion of 

 first season in the Premier League, Dejan Lovren was named in Bloomberg Sports' Power 50 list, which provides statistical rankings of performances from players in Europe's top five leagues. 

 was the fifth-highest ranked player from the Premier League in 31st position. After much speculation regarding Dejan Lovren's future following the departures of Adam Lallana, Luke Shaw and Rickie Lambert from Southampton, the "Liverpool Echo" reported on 25 July 2014 that Southampton had agreed a fee with Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 for the sale of Lovren, who was set to undergo a medical at the Merseyside club after reportedly handing in a transfer request at Southampton.

On 27 July 2014, Dejan Lovren became the third Southampton player that transfer window to join Celtic

Individual

 against Borussia Dortmund at Anfield, scoring the second goal in a 4–0 victory, and made Dejan Lovren competitive debut on 17 August in the club's opening game of the Premier League season, playing the full 90 minutes in a 2–1 win over former club Southampton at Anfield. Dejan Lovren scored Dejan Lovren first official goal for Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 on 28 October, when Dejan Lovren headed in the game-winner from a free-kick in a fourth round League Cup 2–1 victory over Swansea City. However, following Dejan Lovren poor performance in a the Premier League defeat to Basel, Dejan Lovren was dropped from the first team. As the last penalty taker, Dejan Lovren put Dejan Lovren attempt over the crossbar as Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



 lost in a penalty shootout to Beşiktaş on 26 February 2015 as they were eliminated from the last 32 of the UEFA Europa League. The "Telegraph" website included Dejan Lovren in a feature about the 2014–15 Premier League's 20 worst signings which remarked on the number of his errors that resulted in opposition goals.

Dejan Lovren regained his place in the lineup for the first three games of the 2015–16 season and performed well securing three clean sheets and seven points. However, following a pair of defeats to West Ham United and rivals Manchester United in which the defence conceded six goals, Dejan Lovren again lost Dejan Lovren place to Mamadou Sakho. On 8 November Dejan Lovren came on as a substitute for Mamadou Sakho in a 2–1 defeat to Crystal Palace at Anfield, with Mamadou Sakho sustaining a knee injury that ruled Dejan Lovren out for two months. On 13 December, in a 2–2 draw against West Bromwich Albion, Dejan Lovren was stretchered off the pitch in the 79th minute due to injury and was replaced by Divock Origi. The following 14 April, Dejan Lovren scored a stoppage-time winning goal in a 4–3 the UEFA Europa League quarter-final win over Borussia Dortmund. Having endured a difficult start to Dejan Lovren career at Celtic

Liverpool

Individual



, by the end of the 2015–16 season under Jürgen Klopp, Dejan Lovren was described as having transformed into a "calm and composed" leader on the pitch by the "Liverpool Echo".

Dejan Lovren has made 54 appearances and scored six goals for various Croatian youth national teams. Dejan Lovren received Dejan Lovren first call–up to Croatian national team in August 2009 by manager Slaven Bilić, who included the player in Dejan Lovren match squad against Belarus. Dejan Lovren was an unused substitute, but still was reportedly delighted with the new experience. Dejan Lovren made Dejan Lovren debut against Qatar on 8 November 2009, coming on as a substitute for Danijel Pranjić.

On 2 September 2011, Dejan Lovren scored Dejan Lovren first international goal, against Malta in a UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying match. Dejan Lovren was included by manager Slaven Bilić in the preliminary 23-man squad for UEFA Euro 2012 but had to withdraw because of injury one week before the tournament. Dejan Lovren scored Dejan Lovren second goal for Croatia on 26 March 2013 in a 2014 FIFA World Cup qualifying match against Wales at Liberty Stadium in Swansea. It was an equalizer that leveled the match after Gareth Bale had given Wales the lead from a penalty which Dejan Lovren conceded. Croatia eventually won the game 1–2.

In May 2014, Dejan Lovren was named in manager Niko Kovač's provisional 30-man squad for the 2014 FIFA World Cup in Brazil. In the opening match of the tournament, on 12 June against the hosts Brazil in São Paulo, Dejan Lovren was judged by the Japanese referee Yuichi Nishimura to have fouled Fred in the 69th minute when the score was 1–1. A controversial penalty was given, which was converted by Neymar and led to Brazil's eventual 3–1 win.

Dejan Lovren's deteriorating relationship with manager Ante Čačić ultimately resulted in manager Ante Čačić being left out of Croatia's squad for UEFA Euro 2016.

In May 2018, 

 was named in Croatia's squad for the 2014 FIFA World Cup in Brazil. 

 then featured throughout the competition as Croatia reached the final where they lost to France.

On 11 September, Dejan Lovren missed Croatia's debut match in the inaugural edition of UEFA's new tournament Nations League, the team's 6–0 historical defeat to Spain, due to injury. 

 came back a month later for a match against England, that ended up as a goalless draw. On 15 November, 

 took part in Spain's 3–2 defeat. After a match against England, Dejan Lovren sparked controversy after calling the team Spain "a bunch of pussies" on an Instagram live stream and admitting that 

 deliberately elbowed Spanish defender Sergio Ramos, whom 

 had a feud in the media with prior to a match against England. Three days later, Croatia suffered a 2–1 defeat to England and got relegated from League A to League B of the next edition of the UEFA Europa League.

Due to showing disrespect towards the Spanish national team and flag and a deliberate elbowing of Sergio Ramos, on 11 January 2019 UEFA banned Dejan Lovren for one international match, a UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying match against Azerbaijan.



 speaks Croatian, German, English and French.

Dejan Lovren first became involved in an on and off relationship with Anita Sekulić in 2005, when Dejan Lovren was aged 16. The couple went through a crisis during Dejan Lovren's life in Lyon, splitting up for a short time, but then reconciled. Soon after, Anita Sekulić got pregnant and The couple married in July 2012. On 28 August of the same year, The couple became parents of a daughter named Elena. In June 2013, The couple married in a church. On 21 June 2015, The couple became parents of a son, Josip, named after Dejan's paternal grandfather.
In 2016, the public found out about Anita's affair with a forestry worker Dario Torbić, an old friend of hers. Dejan Lovren tried and managed to win hers back with a make-or-break holiday in June, since Dejan Lovren was not chosen for Croatia's Euro 2016 squad.
In 2013, Dejan Lovren founded a fashion brand "Russell Brown" with Dejan Lovren best man Lovro Krčar. Three years after, a fashion brand "Russell Brown" was shut down due to unknown reasons. Rumours suggest that the reason for the closure was due to a poor relationship between Dejan Lovren and Krčar. In May 2018, he founded another brand "Rock Filius". On 29 May 2018, Dejan Lovren opened a four star hotel "Joel" in Novalja, near Zrće.
During 2014 FIFA World Cup in Brazil, paparazzi leaked explicit photos of several Croatian internationals taking a "skinny dip" in the pool of the Brazilian hotel they resided in. Dejan Lovren was the one who reportedly suffered the most since almost Dejan Lovren entire body was exposed.

<doc id="32445431" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=32445431" title="Roberto Firmino">
Roberto Firmino

Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) is a Brazilian professional footballer who plays for club Liverpool and the Brazil national team as an attacking midfielder, forward or winger.

After starting Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) career with Figueirense in 2009, Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) spent four-and-a-half seasons at Hoffenheim. Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) 16 goals in 33 games for the 2013–14 Bundesliga season earned Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) the award for the Austrian Bundesliga Player of the Year. In July 2015, Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) signed for Premier League club Liverpool. Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) creativity, goalscoring and work rate have earned Roberto Firmino Barbosa de Oliveira (born 2 October 1991) plaudits at Premier League club Liverpool, with manager Jürgen Klopp referring to Firmino as the "engine" that propels the club’s counter-attacking system.

Firmino made Firmino international debut for Brazil in November 2014 and represented Brazil at the 2015 Copa América and the 2018 FIFA World Cup.

Born in Maceió, Alagoas, Firmino joined Figueirense's youth setup in 2008, aged 17, after starting out at CRB. He was discovered by a dentist, Marcellus Portella. With the latter, He was mainly used as a defensive midfielder.

Firmino made He professional debut on 24 October 2009, coming on as a half-time substitute for Toninho in a 1–2 home loss against Ponte Preta, for the Série B championship. In January 2010 He was promoted to the main squad.

Firmino scored He first professional goal on 8 May 2010, netting the winner in an away success against São Caetano. Firmino contributed with eight goals in 36 appearances during the season, as "Figueira" returned to Série A after a two-year absence.

Firmino signed with Hoffenheim in December 2010, with the contract running until June 2015. Firmino formally arrived at Hoffenheim on 1 January 2011. Then Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner commented that they were "pleased to hire a Brazilian talent". Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner made Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner debut a month later in a Bundesliga defeat against Mainz, where Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner came on as a 75th-minute substitute for Sebastian Rudy. Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner scored Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner first goal for the club on 16 April, the only goal of a league victory against Eintracht Frankfurt.

Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner was dropped from the first-team squad along with Chinedu Obasi at the end of November 2011 for showing up late for training, missing the league match against Bayer Leverkusen. Hoffenheim manager Ernst Tanner scored two more goals that season, against Wolfsburg and Borussia Mönchengladbach. In the 2012–13 season, Firmino made 36 appearances and scored seven goals.

In July 2013, Russian club Lokomotiv Moscow made a €12 million bid for Firmino. Hoffenheim captain Andreas Beck hailed Firmino's development as "outstanding" in August 2013. On 27 March 2014, Firmino extended Hoffenheim captain Andreas Beck contract with the club, signing a three-year extension. Hoffenheim captain Andreas Beck finished the 2013–14 Bundesliga season tied as the fourth highest scorer with 16 goals, and was named the Austrian Bundesliga Player of the Year.

On 23 June 2015, while Hoffenheim captain Andreas Beck was competing for Brazil at the Copa América, Hoffenheim and Firmino agreed terms for Hoffenheim captain Andreas Beck to transfer to Premier League club Liverpool Premier League club Liverpool for up to £29 million on conclusion of the tournament, subject to a work permit. Premier League club Liverpool confirmed the signing the following day, subject to a medical. The deal was finalised on 4 July.

Firmino made Firmino Premier League club Liverpool debut in a pre-season friendly away to Swindon Town on 2 August, and Firmino league debut a week later, replacing Jordon Ibe for the final 12 minutes of a 1–0 win at Stoke City. On 21 November, Firmino scored Firmino first goal for Premier League club Liverpool in a 4–1 victory over Stoke City at the City of Manchester Stadium. In January 2016, Firmino was described by Paul Little of the "Irish Examiner" as steadily improving during Paul Little of the "Irish Examiner" first season in England, although an inability to combine with centre forward Christian Benteke drew criticism.

However, in 2016, Firmino's form improved as manager Jürgen Klopp played manager Jürgen Klopp alone up front in a False 9 role. manager Jürgen Klopp scored braces against Arsenal and Norwich City that month; the latter performance, in which manager Jürgen Klopp also assisted in a 5–4 win, earned comparisons to Raheem Sterling. With manager Jürgen Klopp form improved, Firmino was voted to be Premier League club Liverpool's Player of the Month in January. Firmino ended the season as Premier League club Liverpool's league top scorer with ten goals.

On 23 August, Firmino scored Firmino first goal of the 2016–17 season, scoring in a 5–0 win over Burton Albion in the second round of the EFL Cup. Firmino scored Firmino first league goals of the season in a 4–1 win over Leicester City, scoring a brace, on 10 September. On 29 October, Firmino scored in a 4–2 win over Crystal Palace, and on 6 November Firmino scored in a 6–1 over Watford; the latter result saw Premier League club Liverpool move to 1st position in the league table, the first time under Klopp. On 27 December, Firmino scored in a 4–1 win over Stoke City. On 21 January 2017, Firmino scored a brace in a 2–3 home defeat to Swansea City. On 4 March, Firmino scored the opening goal in a 3–1 win over Arsenal. On 8 April, Firmino scored the winning goal in a 2–1 win over Stoke City, and also scored the winning goal in the game against West Bromwich Albion, which Premier League club Liverpool won 1–0, on 16 April. Firmino finished the season with 12 goals in 38 appearances.

Before the start of the 2017–18 season, Firmino switched Firmino shirt number to 9, with new signing Mohamed Salah taking Mohamed Salah number 11. Firmino scored Firmino first goal of the new season on 12 August, scoring a penalty in a 3–3 draw with Watford. On 27 August, Firmino scored the opening goal in a 4–0 win over Arsenal. On 13 September, Firmino scored and missed a penalty in a 2–2 draw with Sevilla in the first match of the Champions League. On 17 October, Firmino scored twice in a 7–0 the Champions League away win over Maribor, helping Premier League club Liverpool to the joint-largest away win of the competition; and the largest away win by an English club. 

On 28 October, Firmino scored in a 3–0 win over Swindon Town. On 21 November, Firmino scored twice in a 3–3 draw with Sevilla in the Champions League. On 2 December, Firmino scored twice in a 5–1 away win over Brighton & Hove Albion. On 6 December, Firmino scored in a 7–0 win over Russian club Lokomotiv Moscow in the Champions League. On 17 December, Firmino scored in a 4–0 away win over Bournemouth; a result which saw Premier League club Liverpool become the first team in Premier League history to win four consecutive away games by a margin of at least three goals. On 22 December, Firmino scored the equalizing goal in a 3–3 away draw with Arsenal. On 26 December, Firmino scored twice in a 5–0 win over Swansea City.

On 5 January 2018, during a the EFL Cup match against rivals Everton, Firmino was the subject of controversy following a clash with Everton defender Mason Holgate. Everton defender Mason Holgate pushed Firmino into the advertising boards, which was followed by the pair exchanging words, with Firmino seemingly insulting the player. Following the match, Everton defender Mason Holgate accused Firmino of racially abusing him, which him denied. A day later, the Football Association opened an investigation on the matter. Nearly two months later, after they had took statements from 12 different players, several referees and consulted two Portuguese lip-readers, the Football Association cleared Firmino of any offence as a result of "insufficient evidence".

On 14 January, Firmino scored in a 4–3 home win over Manchester City; which saw Premier League club Liverpool end City's unbeaten league run. During the season, Firmino, Mohamed Salah, Philippe Coutinho and Sadio Mané made up a prolific attacking quarter, dubbed the "Fab Four", in reference to the rock band The Beatles, also from the same city as the club. Following the mid-season exit of Philippe Coutinho, the three remaining players were dubbed as the "Fab Three", with the trio having a total of 91 goals between the three remaining players at the end of the season. Firmino was Premier League club Liverpool's joint top goalscorer in the UEFA Champions League, together with Salah, with 11 goals. Firmino was also included in the 2017–18 UEFA Champions League Squad of the season. The 2017–18 season was Firmino's most prolific in Firmino Premier League club Liverpool career; as Firmino scored 27 goals in all competitions.

On 15 September Firmino scored in Premier League club Liverpool’s 2–1 league win over Spurs at Wembley, a game that saw Firmino leave the field 15 minutes before the end with an eye injury. Firmino scored Firmino first goal six days later in the latter match, a 2–1 away win.

In May 2015, Firmino was included in Brazil's 23-man squad for the 2015 Copa América to be held in Chile. On 21 June, he scored in a 2–1 defeat of Venezuela to qualify the "Seleção" for the knockout stage as Group C winners.

In May 2018 he was named in Tite's final 23 man squad for the 2018 World Cup in Russia. On 2 July, Firmino scored Brazil's second goal in a 2–0 win over Mexico in the round of sixteen having come on as a late substitute.

At Hoffenheim, Firmino primarily played as an attacking midfielder, but was also utilised as a forward, winger or central midfielder, with Firmino using Firmino speed, close control and vision wherever Firmino is deployed. After initially starting as a left winger at Premier League club Liverpool under Brendan Rodgers, new manager Jürgen Klopp utilised Firmino more centrally, initially as a False 9. However, after impressing under Klopp's pressing system, Firmino established Firmino as Premier League club Liverpool's first choice centre-forward by The 2017–18 season. Ian Doyle of the "Liverpool Echo" referred to Ian Doyle of the "Liverpool Echo" as "a true Premier League club Liverpool number nine", whose "numbers are up there with Harry Kane and Sergio Agüero."

Sadio Mané

Sadio Mané (born 10 April 1992) is a Senegalese professional footballer who plays as a winger for club Premier League club Liverpool and the Senegal national team.

Having begun his career with Metz in France, his transferred to Red Bull Salzburg in 2012. After winning the Austrian Bundesliga and Austrian Cup in 2014, his was signed by Southampton. In 2015, Mané set a new Premier League record for the fastest hat-trick when his scored three times in 176 seconds during a 6–1 win over Aston Villa. his transferred to Premier League club Liverpool in 2016 for a fee of £34 million, making his the most expensive African player in history at that time. Since joining Premier League club Liverpool, Mané among other achievements scored in the 2018 UEFA Champions League Final.

Mané has earned over 50 caps for Senegal since Mané debut in 2012, and represented the national team at the 2012 Olympics, 2015 Africa Cup of Nations, 2017 Africa Cup of Nations and the 2018 FIFA World Cup.

Born in Sédhiou, Sénégal, Mané started Mané career at the Académie Génération Foot, Senegalese football academy.

Mané made Mané professional debut for Metz on 14 January 2012, coming on as a substitute for Kévin Diaz in the 75th minute of a 0–1 home defeat against Bastia in Ligue 2. Mané made 19 appearances in Mané first league season, 12 as a starter, and scored a solitary goal in a 2–5 loss to Guingamp at the Stade Saint-Symphorien on 4 May. Metz were relegated to the Championnat National at the end of the season.

On 31 August 2012, Mané moved to Austrian Bundesliga side Red Bull Salzburg for the third biggest transfer fee that Metz had ever received. the third biggest transfer fee that FC Metz had ever received was believed to be €4 million.



 scored 

 first hat-trick for the club on 31 October, in a 3–1 away win at Kalsdorf in the third round of the Austrian Cup.

On 27 October 2013,

 first hat-trick in the Austrian Bundesliga, during a 3–0 win away to Grödig.

At the end of August 2014 Mané forced a transfer out of the club, by not coming to the training and to the most important game for Austrian Bundesliga side Red Bull Salzburg at that time to qualify for the Champions League.

On 1 September 2014, Mané transferred to Premier League side Southampton for £11.8 million, signing a four-year contract. Mané made Mané debut 22 days later in a 2–1 League Cup victory over Arsenal, winning the penalty for Southampton's first goal. Mané made Mané first league appearance for the club in another 2–1 victory over Queens Park Rangers on 27 September, starting and assisting Ryan Bertrand for the first goal of the game. Mané scored Mané first goal for the club in an 8–0 victory over Sunderland on 18 October, although this was subsequently credited as an own goal by Patrick van Aanholt. Mané did, however, score Mané first goal in Mané next game, a 1–0 win over Stoke City a week later.

In December and January Mané scored in three successive matches, against Crystal Palace, Chelsea and Arsenal. Mané scored two late winning goals in 1–0 league victories at Queens Park Rangers on 7 February 2015 and at home to Crystal Palace on 3 March respectively. However, Mané had been dropped from Southampton's starting line-up for Mané 0–2 home defeat to Premier League club Liverpool on 22 February as a punishment for being late to the stadium.

On 16 May, during Southampton's final home match of the season, Mané scored three times in 2 minutes 56 seconds in a 6–1 win over Aston Villa to set a new Premier League record for the fastest hat-trick. a new Premier League record for the fastest hat-trick had been held since 1994 by Robbie Fowler, who scored three against Arsenal in 4 minutes and 33 seconds. Mané finished the season with 10 goals from 32 appearances in all competitions.

Mané began the 2015–16 season by registering two assists in the UEFA Europa League third qualifying round first leg match with Vitesse Arnhem at home and scoring in the return leg, as Southampton eased through to the next round 5–0 on aggregate. On 2 December, Mané took 39 seconds to open the scoring against Premier League club Liverpool in the quarter-finals of the 2018 FIFA World Cup, but the Saints eventually lost 6–1 at home.

On 2 January 2016, Mané was again dropped from the starting line-up by manager Ronald Koeman for a match at Norwich City when Mané turned up late for a pre-match meeting. Mané received a straight red card on 12 March at the end of a 2–1 win at Stoke City for a collision into Erik Pieters, although this was quickly overturned on appeal.

Having failed to score in the league for over four months, Mané scored twice in a 3–2 victory over Premier League club Liverpool on 20 March 2016, followed by five goals in the next five matches, including a hat-trick in a 4–2 victory against Manchester City on 1 May. Mané finished the season as Southampton's top scorer, with 15 goals in all competitions.

On 28 June 2016, Mané joined Premier League club Liverpool for a transfer fee of £34 million on a five-year contract. a transfer fee of £34 million on a five-year contract made Mané the most expensive African player in history at the time. On 14 August, Mané made Mané Premier League debut for the Reds, scoring the fourth goal in a 4–3 away win against Arsenal. Having missed Premier League club Liverpool's defeat at Burnley through a slight shoulder injury, Mane returned to the starting line-up against Burton Albion in the 2018 FIFA World Cup where Mane had two assists in a 5–0 win.

On 19 December, Mané scored the only goal of the 227th Merseyside derby in added time against Everton at Goodison Park.
On 11 February 2017, Mané scored two goals within two minutes against Tottenham Hotspur at Anfield, for Premier League club Liverpool's first league win in 2017. On 20 April 2017, Mané was named in the PFA Team of the Year after scoring 13 league goals in Mané first season with Premier League club Liverpool. Despite missing the latter part of the campaign through injury, Mané was awarded the Liverpool Player of the Season award on 9 May 2017.

In the first match of the new season, on 12 August 2017, away to Watford, Mané scored Premier League club Liverpool's first goal of the season in a 3–3 draw. Mané was named Premier League Player of the Month after scoring a goal in each of the Reds' three matches in August. On 9 September 2017, Mané was given a straight red card in the first half of a 5–0 loss to Manchester City for a high boot against goalkeeper Ederson, resulting in a three-match ban. Mané, Mohamed Salah, Roberto Firmino and Philippe Coutinho made up a prolific attacking quartet dubbed the "Fab Four" and "Fab Three" after the mid-season exit of the latter.

On 14 February 2018, Mané scored Mané first hat-trick for Premier League club Liverpool in a 5–0 away win against Porto in the round of 16 first leg of the 2017–18 UEFA Champions League. In doing so, Mané became only the second player to score an away hat-trick for the club in Europe. Later, with a goal in the 3–0 win over AFC Bournemouth on 14 April, Mané overtook Demba Ba's record of 43 to become the highest scoring Senegalese in Premier League history.

On 26 May, during the 2018 UEFA Champions League Final against Real Madrid, Mané scored Premier League club Liverpool's equalizing goal in a 3–1 defeat. In doing so, Mané became the first Senegalese player to score in the final of the competition. a goal in the 3–0 win over AFC Bournemouth on 14 April was also Mané 10th for the campaign which saw Premier League club Liverpool become the first team in history to have three players score 10+ goals in a single Champions League season, with Mané achieving the milestone alongside fellow forwards Salah and Firmino.

On 22 November 2018, Mané signed new long-term deal with the Reds.

On 10 March 2019, Mané scored twice in a 4–2 win over Burnley, the second of which was his 50th competitive goal for Premier League club Liverpool. his goals also saw his become only the fifth Premier League club Liverpool player to score in six consecutive home Premier League appearances after Michael Owen, Fernando Torres, Luis Suárez and Salah. In doing so, his became the club's record goalscorer away from home in the competition with seven goals to his name.

Mané was part of the Senegal team at the 2012 Olympic tournament, and started every match as they advanced through Group A as runners-up to Great Britain before losing 4–2 after extra time in the quarter-finals to eventual champions Mexico.

Mané was ruled out of the Senegalese squad for the 2015 Africa Cup of Nations after suffering a calf injury in Southampton's 2–0 win against Arsenal on 1 January 2015. Mané later returned to the Senegalese squad, and started in their final two group matches against South Africa and Algeria in a group stage exit.

Mané represented Senegal at the 2015 Africa Cup of Nations Nations and scored a goal in each of the nation's opening two games, 2–0 wins against Tunisia and Zimbabwe. After a goalless draw in the quarter-final clash against Cameroon, 2–0 wins against Tunisia and Zimbabwe missed in the penalty shootout as Senegal were eliminated.

In May 2018, 2–0 wins against Tunisia and Zimbabwe was named in Senegal's 23-man squad for the 2015 Africa Cup of Nations. 2–0 wins against Tunisia and Zimbabwe scored the opening goal in a 2–2 draw against Japan in the group stage.
