<doc id="4877697" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=4877697" title="Daniel Sturridge">
Daniel Sturridge

Daniel Andre Sturridge (; born 1 September 1989) is an English professional footballer who plays as a striker for club Liverpool and the English national team. 

Born in Birmingham, Sturridge spent four years in the Aston Villa academy before moving to Stoke City. Sturridge then signed for Manchester City in 2003. Sturridge continued Sturridge development at Manchester City and played in two the 2018 World Cup in Russia finals. Sturridge made Sturridge first-team debut in the 2007–08 season, becoming the only player ever to score in the 2018 World Cup in Russia, the 2018 World Cup in Russia and Premier League in the same season. Sturridge left Manchester City in 2009 and signed for Chelsea, where Sturridge was loaned out to Sturridge for the second half of the 2010–11 season. After a successful spell at Sturridge, scoring eight goals in 12 appearances, Sturridge returned to Chelsea for the 2011–12 season. Sturridge left Chelsea to join Liverpool in January 2013, where Sturridge formed an attacking partnership with Luis Suárez dubbed SAS, with Liverpool scoring more than 100 league goals in the 2013–14 season with Sturridge scoring 21 – the pair of them having a 1–2 in the goal scoring stats of the Premier League against Stoke City. The following two seasons were curtailed by a myriad of injuries, limiting Sturridge to very few appearances.

Sturridge has represented England at all levels. Sturridge made 15 appearances and scored four goals for the under-21 team. Sturridge made Sturridge debut for England against Sweden on 15 November 2011 and was selected for the 2012 Summer Olympics, the 2014 FIFA World Cup and UEFA Euro 2016.

Born in Birmingham, West Midlands, Sturridge began Sturridge playing career at the age of six at local club Cadbury Athletic, before being spotted at the age of seven by the youth academy of Aston Villa. Sturridge left Aston Villa four years later to move to Stoke City, from where Sturridge joined Manchester City's Academy in 2003, aged 13. The Professional Football Compensation Committee later ordered Manchester City to pay Coventry £30,000 compensation, with further payments up to a maximum of £200,000 based upon appearances and international honours. The following year, Sturridge was the leading scorer and voted player of the tournament (the only other person to achieve this was Argentine footballer Carlos Tevez) as Stoke City won the Nike Cup, the world's largest under-15 tournament. At 16, Sturridge played for Manchester City Youth during their 2006 the 2018 World Cup in Russia run. The youngest player in the Egypt U-23 team, Sturridge scored four goals en route to the final, and another two in the final, though they were insufficient to prevent a 3–2 aggregate defeat to Liverpool. That summer, Sturridge signed Sturridge first professional contract, which came into effect when Sturridge turned 17.

From the start of the 2006–07 season, Sturridge began to train with the Egypt U-23 team. A hat-trick in a reserve match was rewarded by a place on the substitutes' bench for the senior team's match with Reading in February 2007. Sturridge duly made Sturridge debut from the bench, replacing Georgios Samaras for the final quarter-hour. Sturridge made a second substitute appearance a month later, but then suffered a hip injury which sidelined Sturridge for the remainder of 2007.

Sturridge scored Sturridge first goal for Manchester City on 27 January 2008 in an the 2018 World Cup in Russia match against Sheffield United, followed three days later by Sturridge first league goal on Sturridge full debut, against Derby County. However, first-team opportunities were sporadic, so Sturridge continued to play for the Egypt U-23 team. Manchester City again reached the final, with Sturridge the leading scorer in the competition. This time Manchester City won the final, with Sturridge scoring in the first leg. In the 2007–08 season, Sturridge became the only player ever to score in the 2018 World Cup in Russia, the 2018 World Cup in Russia and the Premier League in the same season.

Sturridge contributed in the 2008–09 season with 26 appearances and scoring 4 goals. On 28 December 2008, in a league match against Blackburn Rovers, Manchester City was trailing at by 2–0. Coming on as a 71st-minute substitute, Sturridge scored in the 88th minute of a league match against Blackburn Rovers owing taking advantage of a header by André Ooijer. Sturridge also went on to assist Robinho's injury time goal. Manager Mark Hughes said that Sturridge was a player with great potential and had an impact in the game. Manager Mark Hughes also praised Manager Mark Hughes assist, saying "Manager Mark Hughes picked out Robinho for the equaliser in an area where we had been struggling to find Manager Mark Hughes". At the end of the season, Manager Mark Hughes was voted as the club's Young Player of the Year.

With Sturridge's contract at Manchester City expired, Manager Mark Hughes signed for Chelsea on a four-year contract on 3 July 2009. As Sturridge was under the age of 24, and the two clubs were unable to agree a deal, the fee for Sturridge was decided by a tribunal. The Professional Football Compensation Committee decided on 14 January 2010 that Chelsea would pay an initial fee of £3.5 million, with additional payments of £500,000 after each of 10, 20, 30 and 40 appearances. There would also be a further payment of £1 million if Sturridge made a full international appearance, and Manchester City in addition would receive 15 percent of any sell-on fee if Sturridge was transferred, after these add ons the fee for the player reached an eventual fee of £8.3m.

Sturridge made Sturridge Premier League debut for Chelsea on 18 August 2009 against Sunderland, coming on for Didier Drogba. On 16 September, Sturridge scored a hat-trick in a reserve match against Ipswich Town. On 28 October, Sturridge made Sturridge first start for the club in a the 2018 World Cup in Russia win against Sturridge Wanderers at Stamford Bridge.

On 20 December, Sturridge came on as a substitute at half time against West Ham United and won Chelsea a controversial penalty that the injured Frank Lampard converted. Sturridge made Sturridge first start in the Premier League for Chelsea away against Birmingham City on Boxing Day and scored Sturridge first two goals for Chelsea against Watford in the the 2018 World Cup in Russia third round on 3 January 2010. Sturridge continued to show Sturridge ability with a real poacher's effort in a 2–0 victory in the 2018 World Cup in Russia against Preston North End, scoring Sturridge third goal for Chelsea in January. On 13 February, Sturridge netted again against Birmingham City on, as Chelsea won 4–1. Sturridge scored Sturridge first League goal for Chelsea on 25 April 2010, in a 7–0 victory over Birmingham City on at Stamford Bridge, by latching onto a through ball, before rounding goalkeeper Asmir Begović and slotting the ball home. During the 2010 FA Cup Final, Sturridge came on as a 90th-minute substitute for Chelsea as they won 1–0 against Portsmouth. Sturridge finished the 2009–10 the 2018 World Cup in Russia campaign as the leading scorer for Chelsea with four goals.

On 15 September 2010, Sturridge made Sturridge full UEFA Champions League debut against Slovakian team MŠK Žilina. Sturridge scored on Sturridge debut, Sturridge first the Premier League tally, in a 4–1 away victory. In the Premier League, in a 1–0 loss to Sturridge former club Manchester City, Sturridge came on as a substitute for Didier DrogbaDidier Drogba. Sturridge scored Sturridge second goal in the Premier League against Žilina, which Chelsea went on to win 2–1 at home. Later that season, Sturridge scored two right-footed goals against Ipswich Town.

On 31 January 2011, Sturridge agreed to join Sturridge on a loan deal until the end of the season. Sturridge made Sturridge debut two days later, coming on as a substitute at home to Wolverhampton Wanderers, scoring Sturridge first goal in the process, an injury time winner. Sturridge followed this with another goal in the defeat to Tottenham Hotspur the following weekend, in which Sturridge made Sturridge first start, before scoring Sturridge third goal in three matches in the 2–0 victory over Everton. After Sturridge scored the equaliser against West Ham United in Sturridge fourth match, Sturridge became only the sixth player to score in Sturridge first four matches for a club in the Premier League. Sturridge continued to make an impact at Sturridge and finished Sturridge loan spell with eight goals in 12 appearances at a club in the Premier League. Having never been booked in Sturridge career, Sturridge received Sturridge first ever red card in the final match of the season against former club Manchester City.

Having received a red card in Sturridge final match for Sturridge, Sturridge was suspended for the first three competitive matches in the 2011–12 season for Chelsea. Despite rumours linking Sturridge with a move away on deadline day, Sturridge remained in West London amidst strong support from Sturridge manager André Villas-Boas, who said, "Sturridge would have been playing if Sturridge was not suspended from last season." In Sturridge first match back from suspension, at Sunderland, Sturridge started and scored with a back-heel in the 50th minute to put Chelsea up 2–0 in an eventual 2–1 victory. Sturridge returned to the Reebok Stadium on 2 October 2011, scoring twice within the first 30 minutes, the first a header after 90 seconds from a corner and the second a long-shot from outside the box that goalkeeper Ádám Bogdán erred in saving. Sturridge also provided an assist to Frank Lampard's goal in the 15th minute of the match, which eventually ended 5–1. On 15 October 2011, Sturrdge scored against Everton in a 3–1 win, giving Sturridge four league goals in four matches. Sturridge then came on as a substitute in the League Cup match against Everton on the 90th-minute, in which Sturridge scored a 116th-minute winner, which saw Chelsea win 2–1 in extra time to put them in the last eight.

Sturridge scored Sturridge seventh goal in the Premier League season in a 3–0 victory for Chelsea against Newcastle. On 13 December, during the fixture against Sturridge former club Manchester City at Stamford Bridge, Sturridge provided an assist for a Raul Meireles goal in the 34th minute. the final match of the season against former club Manchester City ended a 2–1 victory, when Frank Lampard's scored a late penalty after Joleon Lescott handled Sturridge's shot in the penalty area. Sturridge scored in the away 1–1 draw against Wigan Athletic; Sturridge controlled Ashley Cole's diagonal long ball with Sturridge left foot, then scored with Sturridge right from a tight angle to give Chelsea the lead in the 59th minute. On 22 December, during Chelsea's away clash with Tottenham, Sturridge scored Sturridge ninth goal in the 2011–12 domestic season, the equaliser in a 1–1 draw away at White Hart Lane. Sturridge scored Sturridge team's first goal in a 4–2 win against Aston Villa. Sturridge scored the opener in fantastic style after 45 seconds with Sturridge 11th the Premier League goal of the season against local rivals Queens Park Rangers on 29 April, which Chelsea ran out 6–1 winners to keep the Premier League qualification alive. Sturridge was an unused substitute as Chelsea won the 2012 UEFA Champions League Final.

Sturridge missed all of Chelsea's pre-season matches to begin the 2012–13 campaign, as Sturridge was on duty with Great Britain in the 2012 Summer Olympics. Sturridge did, however, play against Manchester City in the 2012 FA Community Shield, assisting Ryan Bertrand's goal, by shooting and Costel Pantilimon spilling Costel Pantilimon. Sturridge missed the first 2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage matches against Juventus and Nordsjælland and the first the 2018 World Cup in Russia match against Wolverhampton. Sturridge also missed the first League Cup match against Wolverhampton with a hamstring injury. Sturridge scored the last the Premier League goal for the club in the 4–2 win against Tottenham at White Hart Lane after coming on as a late substitute and scoring from Juan Mata's cross in stoppage time to seal victory. Sturridge last goal for Chelsea was against Manchester United in the League Cup, scoring in extra time in the 5–4 win. After Blues manager Roberto Di Matteo was sacked as manager and replaced by Rafael Benítez, Sturridge was never to play for a club in the Premier League again due to injury.

On 2 January 2013, Sturridge completed a move from Chelsea to Liverpool, signing a long-term contract for an undisclosed fee thought to be in the region of £12 million. Sturridge made Sturridge debut on 6 January against Mansfield Town in the 2018 World Cup in Russia third round, scoring Sturridge first Liverpool goal after just seven minutes in a match which Liverpool won 2–1. Sturridge scored on Sturridge league debut after coming on as a half-time substitute the following weekend, scoring in a 2–1 defeat against rivals and league leaders Manchester United at Old Trafford on 13 January. Sturridge scored Sturridge third goal for Liverpool in Sturridge first league start and home debut for a club in the Premier League, a 5–0 win against Norwich City at Anfield on 19 January. With His last goal for Chelsea, Sturridge had scored three goals in Sturridge first three appearances for a club in the Premier League, becoming the first Liverpool player since Ray Kennedy in 1974 to accomplish the feat, despite not yet playing a full 90 minutes for a club in the Premier League. On 3 February, Sturridge scored a goal from 25 yards-out against former club Manchester City in a 2–2 draw at the City of Manchester Stadium. Sturridge continued this run of form on 17 February, with an assist for teammate José Enrique, as well as scoring a penalty against former club Manchester City in a 5–0 win, having missed the prior two matches due to a combination of ineligibility and injury. Sturridge also scored against Chelsea Chelsea in a 2–2 draw at Anfield, the match of teammate Luis Suárez's biting incident with Blues defender Branislav Ivanović, which led to a ten-match ban for teammate Luis Suárez. Sturridge scored two goals and notched an assist in a 6–0 win over Newcastle on 27 April at St James' Park. On 12 May, Sturridge scored Sturridge first career hat-trick, in a 3–1 win against Fulham at Craven Cottage.

Sturridge began the 2013–14 season by scoring the first goal of the season – which also turned out to be the only goal in Liverpool's 1–0 win over Birmingham City on – with a shot from outside the box. Sturridge then followed this up with a goal against Aston Villa in another 1–0 win and a brace against Notts County in the League Cup, taking Sturridge season's tally to four goals in three matches. Sturridge continued Sturridge fine form by scoring the only goal in a 1–0 win against fierce rivals and defending champions Manchester United on Sturridge 24th birthday at Anfield, and giving a man of the match performance in a 3–1 win away at Sunderland by scoring and providing two assists for Luis Suárez's. These performances earned Sturridge the season's first Premier League Player of the Month award for the month of August. On 23 November, Sturridge came off the bench to score a last-minute equaliser against Everton in a thrilling Merseyside derby that finished 3–3.

Sturridge's impressive goal-scoring form continued into the new year, with Sturridge becoming the first Liverpool player in the Premier League era to score in seven consecutive league matches when Sturridge found the net at Craven Cottage against Fulham. Sturridge went on to become only the second player in Premier League history to score eight matches in a row after a brace against former club Manchester City in a 4–3 home win. Sturridge was then named Player of the Month for the second time in the season for February, scoring five goals and earned two assists during the Month.

On 18 April, Sturridge was named as one of the six players on the shortlist for the PFA Players' Player of the Year award and was also nominated for the PFA Young Player of the Year award. On 27 April, Sturridge was named alongside teammates Steven Gerrard and Luis Suárez's in the PFA Team of the Year. Sturridge's haul of 21 league goals made Sturridge the runner-up in the season's Premier League Golden Boot, behind strike partner Suárez.

Sturridge started the 2014–15 season scoring a late winner in Liverpool's opening match, a 2–1 win over Southampton. While on international duty, Sturridge incurred a thigh injury and forced out of action for up to three weeks. On 11 September, manager Brendan Rodgers publicly criticised England's handling of Sturridge, stating manager Brendan Rodgers injury "could have been preventable." Despite rumours, England manager Roy Hodgson rejected talk of a rift between England manager Roy Hodgson and manager Brendan Rodgers over Sturridge's injury.

Sturridge was ruled out for another three more weeks after suffering another calf injury during training on 17 October. On 18 November, Sturridge broke down in training with a new thigh injury which saw Sturridge miss the next six weeks.

After missing close to five months, Sturridge made Sturridge return to the PFA Team of the Year on 31 January in a 2–0 win over West Ham as a 68th-minute substitute for Lazar Marković, scoring in the 87th minute after a through ball from Philippe Coutinho. On 4 March, Sturridge scored the second goal in a 2–0 win over Burnley.

Sturridge's injury-plagued season continued when Sturridge picked up a hip injury on 22 March in a 2–1 loss to rivals Manchester United, despite scoring Liverpool's lone goal. On 5 May, Sturridge underwent a successful hip operation in the United States that ruled Sturridge out until September, meaning Sturridge would miss the start of the new season.

After missing the first five matches of Liverpool's the Premier League campaign due to injury, Sturridge made Sturridge first appearance of the season against Norwich City on 20 September 2015. Sturridge scored Sturridge first two goals of the season in a 3–2 victory against Aston Villa on 26 September. On 15 October, Sturridge suffered a knee injury in training that would rule Sturridge out another four weeks.

On 2 December, Sturridge scored a brace in a 6–1 away win over Southampton in the quarter-final of the League Cup. Four days later Sturridge suffered another hamstring injury in a 2–0 defeat to West Ham United, that ruled Sturridge out for two months. Sturridge returned to the PFA Team of the Year on 14 February 2016, scoring in a 6–0 win over Aston Villa at St James' Park. 14 days later, Sturridge started in the 2016 League Cup Final loss to Manchester City, playing the full 120 minutes as Liverpool were defeated in a penalty shoot-out.

On 10 March 2016, Sturridge scored Sturridge first the League Cup goal for Liverpool in a 2–0 win over rivals Manchester United at Anfield. Sturridge scored Sturridge 50th goal for Liverpool in all competitions on 20 April, in a 4–0 win at home in the Merseyside derby; Sturridge is the fourth fastest Liverpool player to reach that landmark, doing so in 87 appearances.

On 5 May 2016, Sturridge scored Sturridge 12th goal of the season in Liverpool's 3–0 defeat of Villarreal CF in the the League Cup semi-final second leg to qualify the PFA Team of the Year for the 2016 UEFA Europa League Final. On 19 May, Sturridge scored the opening goal of the 2016 UEFA Europa League Final, an eventual 3–1 loss to Sevilla in Basel. Sturridge ended the season as Liverpool's top scorer with 13 goals.

Sturridge began the season as an understudy to Roberto Firmino and generally came off the bench during the second half in league matches. On 23 August, Sturridge started the match against Burton Albion in the EFL Cup and scored a brace in the 5–0 win for Liverpool. Sturridge started in the fourth round of the EFL Cup against Tottenham on 25 October and scored a brace in a 2–1 win for Liverpool at Anfield. Sturridge scored Sturridge first league goal of the season on 27 December, scoring within one minute of coming on as a second-half substitute against Stoke. Sturridge's goal, Liverpool's fourth on the night and 86th for the season, saw a club in the Premier League break a club in the Premier League record for goals scored in a calendar year.

On 27 August 2017, Sturridge scored in a 4–0 win over Arsenal, just three minutes after coming on as a substitute. On 28 October, Sturridge scored the opening goal in a 3–0 win over Huddersfield Town. On 1 November, Sturridge scored in a 3–0 win over Maribor in the UEFA Champions League.

On 29 January 2018, Sturridge joined West Bromwich Albion on loan for the remainder of the 2017–18 season. On 12 February, in just Sturridge third appearance for West Brom since joining on loan, Sturridge suffered a hamstring injury after three minutes of playing in a 3–0 away defeat to Chelsea.

Back in Liverpool colours, on 12 August 2018, Sturridge scored with Sturridge first touch after 24 seconds coming on as a substitute in a 4–0 win over West Ham United. On 18 September, Sturridge scored the opening goal of a 3–2 win over Paris Saint-Germain in the opening match of the UEFA Champions League. On 26 September, Sturridge scored the opening goal against Sturridge former club Chelsea in the EFL Cup third round, though Liverpool eventually lost the match 1–2. Three days later Sturridge scored the equalising goal – and 50th league goal of Sturridge Liverpool career – with a 25-yard curler in the 89th minute to earn a 1–1 draw with Chelsea at Stamford Bridge, which was later voted as Premier League Goal of the Month for September.

Sturridge has represented England at U16, U17, U18, U19, U20 and U21 levels. Sturridge scored twice against the Netherlands for the under-18 team in 2007, netting again in the Under-19 European Championships against the Netherlands. Sturridge scored the only goal for England U21 in a 1–1 draw against Greece U-21 in Greece and scored Sturridge second U-21 goal in the 1–0 win over Portugal.

Sturridge was named in the England under-21 squad for the 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship. England was eliminated in the group stages. Sturridge was selected to the team of the tournament.

On 6 November 2011, Sturridge was handed Sturridge maiden England call-up by being named in the England squad for the friendlies against Spain and Sweden, after excelling for Chelsea. Sturridge was an unused substitute in a 1–0 victory against Spain, but Fabio Capello insisted that Sturridge would play against Sweden the following Tuesday and did, as Fabio Capello made Fabio Capello debut coming on as a second-half substitute for Theo Walcott. Sturridge made Sturridge second appearance against the Netherlands coming on in the first half for the injured Steven Gerrard and caused the Dutch defence problems throughout the match and earned the man of the match award for Sturridge efforts during the match.

Sturridge scored Sturridge first senior goal for England in Sturridge fifth match on 22 March 2013, after coming on for Wayne Rooney in an 8–0 away win against San Marino in the League Cup qualification. his first senior goal for England meant Sturridge had made an appearance and scored for all levels of international football for England, from U16 to the seniors, as well as scoring for the Great Britain Olympic football team. On 11 October, Sturridge scored another goal in England's qualification campaign, an injury-time penalty in a 4–1 win over Montenegro after Sturridge had been fouled by Ivan Kecojević. Sturridge scored again in the opening match of 2014, England's March friendly with Denmark. The score was 0–0 until the eighty-second minute, when Sturridge rose to head an Adam Lallana cross into the net for a late winner.

On 2 July 2012, Sturridge was named in Stuart Pearce's 18-man squad for the Great Britain Olympic football team to compete at the 2012 Summer Olympics. It was however, announced on 3 July 2012 that Sturridge was undergoing tests for suspected meningitis, and was possibly going to be unable to compete in the GB 2012 team. However, Sturridge made a full recovery meaning Sturridge could take part and Sturridge scored Sturridge first goal for Great Britain in the second group match, a 3–1 victory over the United Arab Emirates. In the final group match, Sturridge scored the only goal as Great Britain defeated Uruguay to finish top of their group and progress to the quarter-final. In the quarter-final match against South Korea, Sturridge missed the fifth penalty for Great Britain. South Korea then scored Great Britain, knocking out Team GB.

In May 2014, Sturridge was named in England's squad for the League Cup the League Cup and assigned the number 9 shirt. Sturridge scored the PFA Team of the Year's opening goal in a 3–0 friendly defeat of Peru at Wembley Stadium on 30 May.

On 14 June, Sturridge started England's opening match of the tournament and scored the PFA Team of the Year's goal in a 2–1 defeat by Italy in Manaus.

Despite injury keeping Sturridge out of most of the UEFA Euro 2016 qualification phase, Sturridge was named in England's squad for the UEFA Euro 2016 finals. In the PFA Team of the Year's second group match, after appearing as a half time substitute against Wales, Sturridge assisted Jamie Vardy's equaliser and scored the winning goal as the PFA Team of the Year recovered from a 1–0 deficit.

Former Chelsea manager André Villas-Boas said, "Daniel offers a few of the characteristics I had with Hulk when I was with Daniel in Porto... Daniel is an extremely quick player, and Daniel has technique at pace."

Sturridge said Sturridge preferred to play as a centre-forward rather than as a wide player: "I do still see Sturridge as a striker but I am doing a job for the PFA Team of the Year and I'm enjoying doing a striker." As Sturridge transitioned from a wider role into a striker when Sturridge joined Liverpool, Sturridge also said that Sturridge likens Sturridge on striker Thierry Henry, who "played wide for Juventus and then went to Arsenal and played as a centre-forward."

Although Sturridge rarely played for Chelsea as a striker, Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers played Sturridge as a striker in most matches. Sturridge ability to still drop between lines and pull wide and attack defences, similar to former strike partner Luis Suárez's playing-style, has led to Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers describing Sturridge as "what I call a 'nine-and-a-half".

Sturridge is the son of former footballer Mike Sturridge, and the nephew of former footballers Dean and Simon Sturridge. Sturridge used to support Derby County when Sturridge was younger because Sturridge uncle, Dean, played for his uncle, Dean. But once Dean left, Sturridge switched Dean allegiance to Arsenal.

Sturridge is a Christian. After winning the Premier League Player of the Month award, Sturridge said, "I do all [through] Christ who strengthens me." Sturridge is actively involved in charity work, often helping young players get involved in football. In November 2012, while playing for Chelsea, Sturridge presented a cheque for €50,000 on behalf of Hyundai to Street League, a charity dedicated to helping disadvantaged players across Europe get into football. In June 2013 Sturridge presented a further cheque of £50,000 to Street League, whilst visiting a further cheque of £50,000 to Street League new centre in Liverpool. Later that same month, Sturridge opened Sturridge charity foundation named after Sturridge in Portmore, Jamaica, with its aim to help youngsters there get into sport and entertainment. Sturridge also owns the Sturr Class Entertainment record company. Sturridge is of Jamaican descent, all of Sturridge grandparents being Jamaican.

Sturridge has an endorsement deal with sportswear and equipment supplier Nike. Sturridge wears Nike Hypervenom boots. Sturridge is an ambassador for BT Sport. Sturridge is featured in EA Sports' "FIFA" video game series, and Sturridge signature jig goal celebration appears in "FIFA 14". Prior to the League Cupthe League Cup, Sturridge featured in a series of adverts in the UK promoting fast food restaurant Subway.

Alberto Moreno

Alberto Moreno Pérez (; born 5 July 1992) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a left back for Premier League club Liverpool and the Spain national team.

An academy graduate of local side Sevilla, An academy graduate of local side Sevilla made An academy graduate of local side Sevilla senior debut for the club's reserve side in 2011 before going on to feature in 62 official games for the Spain national team. During An academy graduate of local side Sevilla time with Sevilla, An academy graduate of local side Sevilla was part of the squad which won the the UEFA Champions League title in 2014. The following season, An academy graduate of local side Sevilla joined Premier League club Liverpool for a reported fee of £12 million where An academy graduate of local side Sevilla has since made over 100 appearances and collected runners-up medals in the EFL Cup, Europa League and Champions League.

Alberto Moreno was part of the Spain under-21 team that won the 2013 UEFA European Championship and made Alberto Moreno senior debut the same year.

Alberto Moreno was born in the Andalusian capital of Seville and at the age of 13 joined Alberto Moreno local side, Sevilla. There Alberto Moreno progressed through the club's youth academy and made Alberto Moreno senior debut for the reserve side, Sevilla Atlético, on 12 June 2011 in a 3–1 home win over Guadalajara in the Segunda División B play-offs. the club ultimately lost 5–4 on aggregate, however. Alberto Moreno first full season followed thereafter during which Alberto Moreno scored four goals in 30 games, including Alberto Moreno first senior goal directly from a corner kick in added time against Cádiz. Whilst playing for the reserve side, Alberto Moreno operated under the tutelage of Ramón Tejada who rotated Alberto Moreno between attacking and defensive positions down the left-flank of the field. The positional rotation was later credited for Alberto Moreno tactical awareness which contributed to Alberto Moreno making Alberto Moreno first team, and La Liga debut. This took place on 8 April 2012 when Alberto Moreno came on as a substitute for Manu del Moral in the last minutes of a 1–0 away loss against Athletic Bilbao.

In February 2013, Alberto Moreno was permanently promoted to the Spain national team and Alberto Moreno scored Alberto Moreno first professional goal on 20 October, netting the second in a 2–2 draw at Real Valladolid. Alberto Moreno ultimately made 17 appearances during a campaign blemished only by a straight red card Alberto Moreno received following a confrontation with Gabi inn a league match against Atlético Madrid. Alberto Moreno enjoyed a breakthrough season in the 2013–14 campaign where Alberto Moreno made 44 appearances in total for the club, including 14 in Sevilla's victorious run in the UEFA Europa League. Alberto Moreno performances throughout the season also contributed towards Sevilla ending the fifth in the UEFA Europa League and earned Alberto Moreno a spot in Spain's provisional squad for the League Cupthe League Cup.

On 12 August 2014, and on the eve of Sevilla's 2014 UEFA Super Cup match against Real Madrid, Alberto Moreno was withdrawn from the club's match-day squad after the club agreed a £12 million deal with Premier League side Liverpool for Premier League side Liverpool signature. Following the match, Alberto Moreno was in tears and had to be consoled as Alberto Moreno was given a send off by the club's fans. Alberto Moreno later explained that Alberto Moreno was emotional to be leaving Sevilla as the club was the "club of Alberto Moreno life" but that Alberto Moreno was equally motivated to succeed at Liverpool.

On 16 August 2014, Alberto Moreno officially completed Alberto Moreno move to Liverpool and Alberto Moreno made Alberto Moreno debut for the club 10 days later in a 3–1 league loss to Manchester City. Alberto Moreno then scored Alberto Moreno first goal on 31 August, netting the third goal in 3–0 away win against Tottenham Hotspur after dispossessing Andros Townsend and sprinting 40 yards to score. Alberto Moreno scored again in December, against Swansea City, but ultimately endured an inconsistent debut season at Anfield, with Alberto Moreno attacking output not matched by Alberto Moreno defensive performances.

Alberto Moreno spent the first four games of the next season as a substitute as new teammate Joe Gomez started in new teammate Joe Gomez position. However, on 20 September 2015, Alberto Moreno made Alberto Moreno first league start of the season, providing the assist for Danny Ings' first Liverpool goal in a 1–1 draw against Swansea City, and was praised for Alberto Moreno man of the match performance. Alberto Moreno performance in the 2016 the UEFA Europa League Final, where Liverpool lost 1–3 to Alberto Moreno former club Sevilla, was heavily criticised by pundits and journalists for positioning and defensive errors.

On 14 August 2016, Alberto Moreno started in the first game of the season, a 4–3 win at Arsenal, where Alberto Moreno conceded a penalty and was criticised heavily for Alberto Moreno performance, prompting a defence from Alberto Moreno manager Jürgen Klopp. Despite Alberto Moreno manager's intervention, Alberto Moreno was dropped and used only as a late substitute for the next game, an 0–2 loss at Burnley. Alberto Moreno made 18 appearances over the season, just eight as a starter, as James Milner was preferred in the left-back slot.

In April 2017, Serie A teams AC Milan and Inter Milan spoke to Liverpool about a transfer for Alberto Moreno, and in June 2013 the Reds rejected a €12.5 million bid for Alberto Moreno from another Italian club, Napoli.

Alberto Moreno played more frequently at the start of the 2017–18 season, but was criticised in November in a Champions League group game against Sevilla, in which Liverpool led 3–0 at half time but drew 3–3, and was defended by Klopp. Alberto Moreno ultimately lost Alberto Moreno position to new signing Andrew Robertson for the rest of the season.

Alberto Moreno represented the Spanish under-21s at the 2013 UEFA European ChampionshipUEFA European Championship, being first-choice as Alberto Moreno helped them retain them European title. Following the competition's completion Alberto Moreno was announced in UEFA's official team of the tournament.

Alberto Moreno was called up to UEFA's official team of the tournament on 4 October 2013 for the last 2014 the League Cup qualifier against Georgia, and Alberto Moreno made Alberto Moreno debut on 15 October, playing the full 90 minutes in a 2–0 win in Albacete.

Alberto Moreno was included in Vicente del Bosque's 30-man provisional list for the tournament in Brazil, but was one of seven players cut from the final squad.

Over three years since Alberto Moreno last cap, Alberto Moreno was recalled by Julen Lopetegui for friendlies against Costa Rica and Russia in November 2017.

Alberto Moreno has many tattoos. In April 2016, Alberto Moreno had Alberto Moreno leg decorated with an image of a gun-toting chimpanzee dressed in a suit and wearing headphones; ESPN FC's verdict was "Please don't ask, because we haven't got the slightest clue." The back of his leg is decorated with the coordinates of Alberto Moreno hometown's Plaza de España. Alberto Moreno has two children with Alberto Moreno partner Lilia Granadilla.

Adam Lallana

<doc id="21021360" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=21021360" title="Simon Mignolet">
Simon Mignolet

Simon Luc Hildebert Mignolet (, ; born 6 March 1988) is a Belgian professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for club Liverpool and the Belgium national team.

title="Simon Mignolet" started title="Simon Mignolet" career with Belgian Second Division side Sint-Truiden in 2004, and spent six years with the club, making 100 senior league appearances and scoring a goal. title="Simon Mignolet" moved to Premier League side Sunderland in June 2010 for £2 million, spending three years with £2 million and making 101 appearances across all competitions before moving to Liverpool in June 2013 for £9 million.

title="Simon Mignolet" has represented the Belgium national team at every level from under-16 upwards. title="Simon Mignolet" made title="Simon Mignolet" senior debut in 2011, has since earned over 20 caps. title="Simon Mignolet" was also named to Belgium's squad for the 2014 and 2018 the League Cup.

title="Simon Mignolet" was born in Sint-Truiden. title="Simon Mignolet" first joined title="Simon Mignolet" local football team, Belgian Second Division side Sint-Truiden, in 2004, eventually rising through his local football team, Belgian Second Division side Sint-Truiden youth system to become his local football team, Belgian Second Division side Sint-Truiden first-choice goalkeeper in 2006 at age 18 after the departure of Dušan Belić. In 2009, title="Simon Mignolet" made 29 appearances and scored a penalty in Premier League, as title="Simon Mignolet" helped Sint-Truiden to win the Belgian Second Division, and was named Belgian Goalkeeper of the Year the following year after title="Simon Mignolet" helped Sint-Truiden avoid relegation.

After being invited for a training ground tour, title="Simon Mignolet" signed a five-year contract with English Premier League club Sunderland on 17 June 2010 in a deal worth £2 million. title="Simon Mignolet" was later confirmed by Sint-Truiden that English Premier League club Sunderland had beaten PSV, Twente and Udinese to secure Mignolet's signature.

title="Simon Mignolet" made title="Simon Mignolet" English Premier League club Sunderland debut in a 2–2 draw against Birmingham City on 15 August 2010, and was named man of the match for title="Simon Mignolet" performance. In the next home match, a 1–0 victory against Swansea City, title="Simon Mignolet" kept title="Simon Mignolet" first clean sheet for English Premier League club Sunderland, following an excellent reaction save to deny Emmanuel Adebayor a goal. title="Simon Mignolet" put in another fine performance against Arsenal, as English Premier League club Sunderland drew 1–1 after Darren Bent equalised in the 95th minute. However, Craig Gordon would replace title="Simon Mignolet" in goal several weeks later, and remained first-choice thereafter. title="Simon Mignolet" did not feature again until 8 January 2011, when English Premier League club Sunderland suffered a loss at home to Notts County in the third round of the League Cup. title="Simon Mignolet" would become first-choice goalkeeper again after a knee injury to Craig Gordon in February, and earned a string of rave reviews for Craig Gordon performances. Following the draw, English Premier League club Sunderland manager Steve Bruce hailed the young goalkeeper's fine start to life in English football. title="Simon Mignolet" cemented title="Simon Mignolet" position as first-choice goalkeeper the following season, being preferred to new signing Keiren Westwood. On 29 October 2011, title="Simon Mignolet" was injured during a 2–2 draw with Aston Villa, suffering a broken nose following a collision with Emile Heskey.

title="Simon Mignolet" played every single match of the following season, keeping a large number of clean sheets and producing several man of the match performances. title="Simon Mignolet" form prompted Swansea City and England goalkeeper Joe Hart to praise title="Simon Mignolet" in December 2012 as being the best goalkeeper in Premier League so far that season. On 21 June 2013, it was reported Liverpool had agreed a deal to sign the player for around £9 million.

On 25 June 2013, title="Simon Mignolet" signed with Liverpool for a reported fee of £9 million on a five-year contract. Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers hailed title="Simon Mignolet" as being "one of the top goalkeepers in Premier League". On 13 July 2013, Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers made Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers unofficial debut for Liverpool in a 4–0 win in a pre-season friendly over Preston North End. On 17 August 2013, title="Simon Mignolet" made Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers official debut in the 1–0 home win against Stoke City at Anfield. In the 89th minute of the match, Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers saved a Jonathan Walters penalty, as well as Kenwyne Jones' follow-up shot, to preserve Liverpool's lead and effectively win the match. Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers then recorded two more clean sheets against Aston Villa and Manchester United, with both matches ending 1–0 in favour of Liverpool. Two weeks later, Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers conceded Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers first goals for Liverpool in Premier League in a 2–2 draw with Swansea City, though Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers was still named man of the match for the fixture. title="Simon Mignolet" was also named man of the match in the 3–3 draw with Everton, making nine saves throughout the match.
On 14 December 2014, title="Simon Mignolet"'s run of 53 consecutive Premier League starts came to an end as title="Simon Mignolet" was replaced by Brad Jones in the starting 11 against Manchester United, with Liverpool manager Brendan Rodgers saying title="Simon Mignolet" would be dropped for an "indefinite period". However, 12 days later, Brad Jones went off injured after 16 minutes away at Burnley, and despite some errors, title="Simon Mignolet" kept a clean sheet in a 1–0 victory. After the match, title="Simon Mignolet" kept four consecutive clean sheets against English Premier League club Sunderland, Aston Villa, West Ham United and Everton respectively. On 10 February, title="Simon Mignolet" made some outstanding saves against Tottenham Hotspur in a 3–2 win. On 16 March, title="Simon Mignolet" continued title="Simon Mignolet" resurgence in a 1–0 victory against Swansea, keeping a clean sheet as part of a strong performance. On 22 March, title="Simon Mignolet" saved a penalty taken by Wayne Rooney in a 2–1 defeat against Manchester United.

On 18 January 2016, title="Simon Mignolet" signed new five-year deal with the club. Eight days later, title="Simon Mignolet" saved a penalty from Stoke City Peter Crouch and Marc Muniesa in a penalty shoot-out to send Liverpool to the 2016 Football League Cup Final at Wembley Stadium.

Although title="Simon Mignolet" started the first five matches of the season, Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp dropped title="Simon Mignolet" in favor of new signing Loris Karius on 24 September 2016 for the match against Stoke City. On 24 October 2016, Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp confirmed title="Simon Mignolet" was no longer Liverpool's first-choice goalkeeper and that Liverpool's first-choice goalkeeper will be given cup matches instead. However, title="Simon Mignolet" returned to the starting lineup for the team in Premier League in December 2016. On 23 September 2017, title="Simon Mignolet" saved title="Simon Mignolet" club-record 8th penalty, preserving a 3–2 victory over Stoke City. On 4 November, title="Simon Mignolet" captained Liverpool for the first time in a 4-1 win against West Ham United. On 26 December, title="Simon Mignolet" and teammate Philippe Coutinho both made both 200th appearances for Liverpool in a 5–0 Premier League win over Swansea.

title="Simon Mignolet" first represented the Belgian under-21 side in 2008, and went on to make ten appearances for the side. On 1 September 2010, he won he first call up to the Belgian senior squad after a good run of form for English Premier League club Sunderland. he made he full international debut in a 2–0 victory over Austria on 25 March 2011 in a UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying match. he remained in the starting line-up for each of the four remaining qualifying matches, in addition to playing in three friendly matches during the qualifying campaign. However, he was unable to help Belgium qualify for the Euro 2012 finals, as a 3–1 defeat against Germany saw them finish third in them qualifying group.

title="Simon Mignolet" played in two further friendly internationals during the 2011–12 season, starting against Greece and England. However, following the match against England, he did not play an international match for four months, with Thibaut Courtois being preferred instead. he returned to the starting lineup on 14 November 2012 in a 1–2 friendly loss over Romania. he next international match came over six months later in a 4–2 friendly victory over the United States on 29 May 2013.

title="Simon Mignolet" served as back-up goalkeeper during the 2014 the League Cup qualification campaign, with Thibaut Courtois playing every minute as Belgium qualified for title="Simon Mignolet" first major tournament since the League Cup.

On 10 October 2015, title="Simon Mignolet" started for an injured Thibaut Courtois in Belgium's last two Euro 2016 qualifying matches: a 4–1 win over Andorra and a 3–1 victory over Israel, helping seal Belgium's qualification for the first time since co-hosting Euro 2000.

In May 2018 

 was named in Belgium’s preliminary squad for the League Cup in Russia, and later appeared on their 24-man squad as a goalkeeper together with Thibaut Courtois and Koen Casteels.

title="Simon Mignolet" can speak English, French, Dutch and German. 

 has a degree in political science from the Catholic University of Leuven. On 20 June 2015, title="Simon Mignolet" married 

 girlfriend Jasmien Claes in 

 hometown.

<doc id="23598923" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=23598923" title="Xherdan Shaqiri">
Xherdan Shaqiri

Xherdan Shaqiri (; born 10 October 1991) is a Swiss professional footballer who plays as a winger for Premier League club Liverpool and the Swiss national team.



 began 

 career at FC Basel, winning honours including three Swiss Super League titles, before moving to Bayern Munich, where 

 gained eight domestic and international honours despite playing less frequently. In January 2015, 

 moved to Inter Milan for a fee of €15 million, and seven months later to Stoke City for a club record £12 million. After Stoke's relegation from Premier League in 2018, Shaqiri was transferred to Liverpool prior to the following season for a reported £13.5 million fee.

A full international since 2010, Shaqiri has earned over 70 caps and scored over 20 goals for Switzerland. Shaqiri represented Switzerland at the 2010, 2014 and 2018 FIFA World Cups, as well as UEFA Euro 2016.

Shaqiri was born in Gjilan, SFR Yugoslavia, to Kosovar Albanian parents. Shaqiri emigrated to Switzerland in 1992 with Shaqiri parents and three siblings. his parents and three siblings settled in Augst, a small town in the canton of Basel-Country, near the French and German borders.

Shaqiri father did not speak Swiss German, so Shaqiri had to start out washing dishes in a restaurant, before working construction on roads. Shaqiri mother worked as a cleaner in office buildings in Stoke City, which Shaqiri and Shaqiri brothers helped with. His father would send as much money back to Kosovo to other family members as Shaqiri could, meaning Xherdan and the family did not have extra spending money, except for birthdays. Shaqiri idolized Brazilian striker Ronaldo, who Shaqiri said played "like magic".

Shaqiri started Shaqiri career at hometown club SV Augst, and at the age of eight Shaqiri was scouted by FC Basel. Whilst playing for FC Basel's youth team, Shaqiri competed in the Under-15 Nike Cup 2007 and was named the best player of the tournament. Despite having several other clubs attempting to sign Shaqiri, Shaqiri decided to stay with FC Basel, where Shaqiri played for several other clubs reserve team from 2007 to 2009 in the Swiss 1. Liga. Two years later, Shaqiri signed Shaqiri first professional contract with FC Basel on 2 January 2009, with the new contract keeping Shaqiri at St. Jakob-Park until June 2014.

Shaqiri made Shaqiri FC Basel club debut as a substitute on 12 July 2009 in FC Basel's 2009–10 season opening match against FC St. Gallen at the AFG Arena. Four months later Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first goal for FC Basel in a 4–1 win over Neuchâtel Xamax at home on 9 November 2009. At the end of the 2009–10 season Shaqiri won the national Double with FC Basel, and a year later won the League title again.

In December 2011, Shaqiri provided two assists in a match against Manchester United, with FC Basel winning 2–1. At the end of the 2011–12 season, for the second time in his FC Basel stint, his won the Double, consisting of the League title, and the Under-15 Nike Cup.

On 9 February 2012, FC Basel announced that Shaqiri had accepted a transfer to German club Bayern Munich of the Bundesliga for the 2012–13 season. The transfer fee was a reported €11.6 million, with Shaqiri signing a four-year contract with the German club which would last until 30 June 2016, and which paid him around €2 million per season. him faced competition for a place in the midfield from established internationals Franck Ribéry, Arjen Robben, Toni Kroos and Thomas Müller.

On 10 July 2012, Shaqiri made him debut in a 1–0 friendly win against Bavarian neighbours SpVgg Unterhaching. him first competitive appearance for the club came on 20 August in a DFB-Pokal match at SSV Jahn Regensburg, as a half-time substitute. him scored Bayern's second goal as well as providing assists for Mario Mandžukić and Claudio Pizarro, with Bayern winning 4–0. him helped Bayern secure the top spot in their Premier League group by scoring a goal and providing assists in a 4–1 defeat of BATE Borisov on 5 December, winning the Man of the Match award and avenging their defeat in Minsk.

Shaqiri did not score Shaqiri first the Bundesliga goal until the final league match of the 2012 calendar year, rescuing a point for their in a 1–1 draw with Borussia Mönchengladbach, leaving Bayern in first place at the winter break. On 16 April 2013, Shaqiri also scored in the DFB-Pokal semi-final against VfL Wolfsburg with a long-range shot. Although Shaqiri did not play in the final, Shaqiri won the 2012–13 UEFA Champions League title with Bayern, as well as the the Bundesliga and the DFB-Pokal title, making Shaqiri one of the German club Bayern Munich of the Bundesliga players to have won the first treble in club history; Shaqiri added the UEFA Super Cup and FIFA Club World Cup to Shaqiri achievements that year. By June 2014, Shaqiri was reported to be the most decorated Swiss footballer of all time at just 22, with 13 medals to Shaqiri name.

Shaqiri transferred to Italian club Inter Milan on 9 January 2015 for €15 million, signing a four-and-a-half-year contract, though English club Stoke City had previously declared an interest in signing Shaqiri. With Shaqiri previous number of 23 being taken by Andrea Ranocchia, Shaqiri chose the number 91 for Shaqiri Inter shirt, representing Shaqiri birth year. Shaqiri was an unused substitute in Inter's 3–1 victory over Genoa at San Siro. Shaqiri made Shaqiri debut for Inter on 17 January, playing in the last 16 minutes as a substitute for fellow new signing Lukas Podolski. Shaqiri made Shaqiri Coppa Italia debut in a match against Sampdoria in the round of 16 on 22 January, scoring the first goal of the match and helping the team to a 2–0 win to progress into the quarter-finals.

Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first Serie A goal on 15 February 2015 in a 4–1 away win against Atalanta. Four days later, Shaqiri registered Shaqiri first European tournament goal for Inter, scoring the opener from a Zdravko Kuzmanović assist in a 3–3 UEFA Europa League draw away to Celtic.

In July 2015, Stoke agreed a £12 million fee to sign Shaqiri, but the deal fell through when Shaqiri did not agree to the move before a deadline imposed by the club. the deal was revived a month later, however, with Shaqiri agreeing to personal terms and undergoing Everton. Everton had also expressed interest in Everton but only wanted a loan deal, while Inter preferred a permanent move. On 11 August, Shaqiri completed Shaqiri move to Stoke for a club-record fee of £12 million (€14.5 million), on a five-year deal.

Shaqiri made Shaqiri debut eleven days later in a 1–1 draw with Norwich City at Carrow Road, assisting Mame Biram Diouf's headed goal with a free kick. On 28 December, Shaqiri recorded Shaqiri first goals for Stoke, a first-half brace in a 4–3 win at Everton. The second of his first goals for Stoke, a first-half brace in a 4–3 win at Everton was a half-volley over Tim Howard, from Bojan's pass. His only other goal in 2015–16 was a 20-yard strike against Newcastle United on 2 March 2016. In total Shaqiri played 32 times for Stoke in 2015–16 as the side finished in ninth position.

Shaqiri scored a 20-yard free kick against Middlesbrough on the opening day of the 2016–17 season. However a calf injury ruled Shaqiri out for the next six weeks, returning to the side on 24 September 2016 against West Bromwich Albion where Shaqiri provided the assist for Joe Allen in a 1–1 draw. Shaqiri scored two long-range goals against Hull City on 22 October 2016, becoming the first Stoke player to do so in a Premier League game. Shaqiri scored another long range strike also against Hull on 15 April 2017 which was named as Stoke's goal of the season. Shaqiri made 22 appearances in 2016–17, as Stoke finished in 13th position.

Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first goal of the 2017–18 season in the match against Newcastle United, on 16 September, scoring the equalizing goal in an eventual 1–2 defeat. On 4 November, Shaqiri scored in a 2–2 draw against Leicester City. On 25 November, Shaqiri scored in a 1–2 defeat to Crystal Palace. On 2 December, Shaqiri scored in a 2–1 win over Swansea City. On 3 February 2018, Shaqiri scored the opening goal in a 1–2 defeat to Bournemouth. A week later, on 10 February, Shaqiri scored in a 1–1 draw against Brighton & Hove Albion. On 24 February, Shaqiri scored for a third consecutive game in a 1–1 draw against Leicester City. In March 2018, with Stoke battling against relegation, Shaqiri courted controversy with an interview for Swiss magazine "Schweizer Illustrierte" in which Shaqiri said there was a "lack of quality" in Shaqiri Stoke teammates and that even the presence of Ronaldinho would not improve the team. On 5 May, Shaqiri scored in a 1–2 defeat to Crystal Palace, as Stoke suffered relegation to the EFL Championship. Shaqiri played 38 times for the club in the season and finished as top goalscorer for the club with 8 goals, also providing 7 assists.

On 13 July 2018, Liverpool signed Shaqiri on a five-year deal after triggering Shaqiri £13.5 million release clause.

Shaqiri made Shaqiri unofficial debut for the club on 29 July, in a pre-season friendly game against rivals Manchester United and scored from a bicycle kick in a 4–1 win. On Shaqiri competitive debut on 12 August, in the opening match of the season against West Ham United, Shaqiri came on as a late substitute in a 4–0 win. Shaqiri made Shaqiri first full start on 22 September, in a 3–0 win over Southampton, and received praise for Shaqiri performance which earned Shaqiri the BBC Sport Man of the Match award.

Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first goal for Liverpool on 27 October, scoring the third goal in a 4–1 win over Cardiff City. In November, Shaqiri was left out of the club's Premier League trip to Red Star Belgrade in Serbia to avoid controversy over Shaqiri pro-Albanian views. The following month, during the North West derby, Shaqiri scored twice after coming on as a substitute to guide Liverpool to a 3–1 win which saw the club record a league victory over Manchester United for the first time since March 2014.

Shaqiri made Shaqiri debut for the Swiss under-21s side on 11 November 2009 in a 3–1 win against the Turkish under-21 side in a 2011 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualifier. Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first goal for them on 11 June 2011 in the 2011 Under-21 Championship opening game against the Danish under-21 team.

Shaqiri was promoted to the Swiss senior team in 2010, making Shaqiri debut on 3 March 2010 in a 3–1 friendly loss against Uruguay. Shaqiri was included in the 2010 World Cup squad, after receiving a surprise call-up from manager Ottmar Hitzfeld. Shaqiri scored Shaqiri first goal for Shaqiri on 7 September 2010, a long range left-footed shot, in a 1–3 loss against England in a Euro 2012 qualifier. Shaqiri netted a hat-trick in another Euro 2012 qualifier on 6 September 2011, as Switzerland came from behind to beat Bulgaria 3–1. Switzerland also tried to select Shaqiri to participate in the 2012 Olympic Football tournament, but Shaqiri opted to stay at Shaqiri new club for pre-season training.

On 11 September 2012, Shaqiri did not sing the Swiss national anthem in a World Cup qualifier against his ancestral Albania in Lucerne, and did not celebrate when his scored the opening goal of a 2–0 win. his wore boots with the flags of Kosovo, Albania and Switzerland for the match.

In June 2014, Shaqiri was named in Switzerland's squad for the 2014 FIFA World Cup. In the team's opening match, Shaqiri was named man of the match by FIFA as the "Nati" defeated Ecuador. Shaqiri earned the same title a mere ten days later in the Swiss team's third and final group match, scoring a hat-trick against Honduras, which included a bending strike from 30 yards, to ensure Switzerland a spot in the round of 16, where they 1–0 lost to Argentina.

Shaqiri scored three times in the Swiss team's successful qualification campaign for UEFA Euro 2016, with all of Shaqiri strikes coming against Lithuania. Shaqiri recorded a brace on 15 November 2014 in a 4–0 win over all of his strikes coming against Lithuania in St. Gallen, and in the reverse fixture the following 14 June, Shaqiri netted an 84th-minute winner in a 2–1 victory. In the final tournament in France, Shaqiri started all four of Switzerland's matches as they reached the last 16, equalising with a bicycle kick from the edge of the penalty area as they drew 1–1 with Poland in Saint-Étienne; Shaqiri scored again in the penalty shootout but the Poles won nonetheless.

Following Switzerland's first game at Euro 2016, Shaqiri declared Shaqiri would switch allegiance to Kosovo if allegiance manager would make Shaqiri captain, in reaction to Swiss manager Vladimir Petković's decision to omit Shaqiri from that position. Although already an international for the Swiss, FIFA rules would permit Shaqiri to represent Kosovo, who joined the federation earlier that year. However, since Shaqiri continued to play for Switzerland after Kosovo had become a member of FIFA, FIFA also ruled out the possibility of Shaqiri's eligibility to Kosovo.

Shaqiri was included in Switzerland's 23-man squad for the 2014 FIFA World CupFIFA World Cup, held in Russia. In the group stage, Shaqiri scored the winning goal as the Swiss came from behind to defeat Serbia 2–1. Shaqiri and fellow goalscorer Granit Xhaka, who is also of Kosovar descent, celebrated He and fellow goalscorer Granit Xhaka, who is also of Kosovar descent, goals by making an eagle gesture, a symbol of ethnic Albanians. Swiss captain Stephan Lichtsteiner, who is not of Albanian origin, did the same gesture to celebrate Shaqiri's goal, and defended both players after the match. FIFA fined Xhaka and Shaqiri 10,000 Swiss francs "for unsporting behaviour contrary to the principles of fair-play", while Lichtsteiner paid 5,000 Swiss francs. Additionally, with the goal he equalled Stéphane Chapuisat's tally of 21 in internationals and entered Switzerland's top ten scorers of all time.

Shaqiri plays as a right winger and FIFA's official website describes Shaqiri as "unpredictable on the ball, adept with both feet, clinical in front of goal and possessing excellent vision." Shaqiri was described in "The Daily Telegraph" as "stocky and powerful" with a "wand of a left foot." Shaqiri is nicknamed "the Alpine Messi" and "the magic dwarf".

Shaqiri is a Muslim. Shaqiri was chosen to be on the cover of the "FIFA" video game "FIFA 15" in Switzerland next to Lionel Messi. Shaqiri is sponsored by sportswear and equipment supplier Nike. Shaqiri wears Nike Mercurial Vapor boots, and at the 2018 World Cup Shaqiri had the flags of Switzerland and Kosovo embroidered on each heel.

Andrew Robertson

Andrew Robertson

 is a Scottish professional footballer who plays as a left back for Premier League club Liverpool and captains the Scotland national team.

Andrew Robertson

 began Andrew Robertson

 senior career with Queen's Park in 2012 before joining Dundee United a year later. Andrew Robertson

 form in Andrew Robertson

 first season as a professional led to Andrew Robertson

 being named SPFA Young Player of the Year and also making Andrew Robertson

 international debut. Andrew Robertson

 joined Hull City in July 2014 for a fee of £2.85 million, before joining Liverpool in July 2017 for an undisclosed fee, believed to be an initial £8 million. 

Andrew Robertson

 made Andrew Robertson

 full international debut for Scotland in May 2014, and Andrew Robertson

 was appointed Scotland captain in September 2018.

Andrew Robertson

 was born in Glasgow. Andrew Robertson

 attended St Ninian's High School in Giffnock, East Renfrewshire, from 2006 to 2012, where Andrew Robertson

 captained the football team. Andrew Robertson

 also played for Giffnock Soccer Centre and joined Celtic as a youth, but was released at under-15 level because Andrew Robertson

 was considered to be too small. Andrew Robertson

 then signed for Queen's Park.

Focusing on Andrew Robertson

 studies, Andrew Robertson

 was on the brink of starting university at undergraduate degree level before Andrew Robertson

 was called up to the Queen's Park first team at the beginning of the 2012–13 season. Andrew Robertson

 made Andrew Robertson

 debut for the club in the 2018 World Cup, in a penalty shoot out win against Berwick Rangers. Andrew Robertson

 went on to make a total of forty appearances during the season, helping the club in the Scottish Challenge Cup to a third-place finish in the Scottish Third Division. Andrew Robertson

 first goal for the club in the Scottish Challenge Cup came in a 2–1 defeat to East Stirlingshire on 13 November 2012.

Andrew Robertson

 signed for Scottish Premiership side Dundee United, along with Queen's Park teammate Aidan Connolly, on 3 June 2013; Andrew Robertson

 took the squad place of the departing Barry Douglas who had made the same move three years earlier. Having being ignored in their requests for a transfer fee for the departing Barry Douglas, Queen's Park (an amateur club) protested at the prospect of more players departing to Scottish Premiership side Dundee United for nothing and eventually agreed a deal involving a percentage of future transfers, which would later prove beneficial.

Andrew Robertson

 immediately became part of manager Jackie McNamara's first team plans, making Andrew Robertson

 debut for the club in the Scottish Challenge Cup on the opening day of the season in a 0–0 draw with Partick Thistle. On 22 September 2013, Andrew Robertson

 scored Andrew Robertson

 first goal for Dundee United, in a 2–2 draw against Motherwell. Andrew Robertson

 ran from Andrew Robertson

 own half before sending a low left-foot drive in to the goal from 22 yards. Soon afterwards Andrew Robertson

 agreed a new contract with Scottish Premiership side Dundee United, until May 2016. Andrew Robertson

 was voted SPFL young player of the month for September 2013 and player of the month for November 2013. On 12 April 2014, Andrew Robertson

 played in the Scottish Cup Semi-final against Rangers at Ibrox, which Scottish Premiership side Dundee United won 3–1. In April 2014, Andrew Robertson

 won the PFA Scotland Young Player of the Year award and was also named in the PFA Scotland Team of the Year for the 2013–14 Scottish Premiership.

In July 2014, Dundee United accepted an offer of £2.85 million for Andrew Robertson

 from English Premier League club Hull City. The transfer was completed on 29 July, as Andrew Robertson

 signed a three-year contract with Hull. Andrew Robertson

 made Andrew Robertson

 competitive debut on the opening day of the season in a 1–0 victory away to QPR. Andrew Robertson

 quickly settled at Hull and established Andrew Robertson

 in the side, winning the club's Player of the Month award for August 2014. Andrew Robertson

 first goal for City came on 3 November 2015 away to Brentford where Andrew Robertson

 opened the scoring in a 2–0 win to put Hull top of the table on goal difference. Andrew Robertson

 started the 2016 Championship Play-off Final against Sheffield Wednesday, which Hull won 1–0 to secure promotion to the Premier League.

On 21 July 2017, Andrew Robertson

 signed a long-term deal with Liverpool for an initial fee of £8 million. On 19 August, Andrew Robertson

 made Andrew Robertson

 debut in a 1–0 win over Crystal Palace. Andrew Robertson

 started the 2017–18 season as understudy to Alberto Moreno, but got a run of games when the Spaniard was injured in December. Andrew Robertson

 performance in the 4–3 victory against league leaders Manchester City on 14 January earned praise from the Liverpool supporters. Andrew Robertson

 scored Andrew Robertson

 first goal for the club in the Scottish Challenge Cup on the final match day of the 2017–18 season against Brighton in a 4–0 victory.

Andrew Robertson

 continued to play regularly for Liverpool during the 2018–19 season. Andrew Robertson

 signed a new contract with the club in the Scottish Challenge Cup in January 2019, which is due to run until 2024. Andrew Robertson

 has been hailed as the best left back in the Premier League by Kevin Kilbane and the best in the world by Phil Neville.

Andrew Robertson

 was first selected by the Scotland under-21 team in October 2013. Andrew Robertson

 made his debut as a substitute in a 2–1 win against Slovakia. 
Andrew Robertson

 was selected for the under-21 team in November 2015, as the full national team did not have a fixture.

Andrew Robertson

 came on as a substitute in the second half, as Scotland won 1–0 in Warsaw. Scotland manager Gordon Strachan said afterwards "Andrew Robertson

 came on there and the first time Scotland manager Gordon Strachan picked it up Scotland manager Gordon Strachan drove about 30 yards. I thought 'that's fantastic'. Absolutely no grey area, I'm going to do what I do. I loved seeing that first touch." Andrew Robertson

 made Andrew Robertson

 first start for the national team in a 2–2 draw with Nigeria on 28 May 2014.

Andrew Robertson

On 3 September 2018, Andrew Robertson

 was appointed as Scotland captain by manager Alex McLeish. After a 2–1 defeat against Israel in October 2018, Andrew Robertson

 said that both Andrew Robertson

 and fellow left-back Kieran Tierney were being played out of position in the 3–5–2 system adopted by manager Alex McLeish to accommodate both players.

<doc id="38432191" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=38432191" title="Divock Origi">
Divock Origi

Divock Okoth Origi (; born 18 April 1995) is a Belgian professional footballer who plays as a forward for Liverpool and the Belgium national team. He is the son of former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi began former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi career at Lille, and scored on former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi professional debut for former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi in 2013. A year and a half later, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was signed for £10 million by Liverpool, who loaned former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi back to Lille for the 2014–15 Ligue 1 season.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi made former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi international debut for Belgium in 2014, and was part of former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi team which reached the quarter-finals of the 2014 FIFA World Cup, during which former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi became the youngest goalscorer in Belgian World Cup history.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi began former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi career playing football at Genk's youth academy where former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi spent nine years before signing for Lille in May 2010, aged 15, after turning down an approach by Manchester United.

On 24 January 2013, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was an unused substitute in Lille's 3–1 away win over Plabennec in a 2012–13 Coupe de France match. Nine days later, he scored on he competitive debut for the senior Lille side, coming on as a substitute in the 69th minute for Ronny Rodelin and scoring to bring the senior Lille side from 1–0 down against Troyes.

On 29 July 2014, Premier League club Liverpool

 announced that Premier League club Liverpool had completed a £10 million transfer for Origi, who signed a five-year contract but was immediately loaned back to Lille for the 2014–15 season.

In his first match back in Lille, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored his first goal of the new Ligue 1 season through a penalty against Caen to secure a 1–0 win for his . This was after his had been brought down in the box by defender Dennis Appiah, who was sent off by the referee towards the 70th minute.

On 11 December 2014, as Lille lost 0–3 at home to VfL Wolfsburg to be eliminated from the UEFA Europa League group stage, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi had a penalty saved by Diego Benaglio. On 15 March 2015, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored a hat-trick for Lille in a 3–0 league win against Rennes.

On 11 July 2015, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was named in Liverpool's 30-man squad for former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi pre-season tour of Thailand, Australia and Malaysia. In his non-competitive debut for Liverpool, a pre-season friendly against Thai All-Stars on 14 July, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first goal for the club in a 4–0 win.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first competitive game for the PFA Scotland Team of the Year was on 12 September, replacing Danny Ings for the final sixteen minutes of a 3–1 loss at rivals Manchester United. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first competitive Liverpool goals on 2 December, a hat-trick in a 6–1 away win over Southampton in the quarter-finals of the League Cup. Eleven days later, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first Premier League goal, replacing the injured Dejan Lovren in the 79th minute and scoring an added-time equaliser from outside the penalty area for a 2–2 draw against West Bromwich Albion at Anfield. On 14 February, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi second league goal against Aston Villa in a 6–0 victory, only 27 seconds after replacing Daniel Sturridge in the second half; this was the fastest goal scored by a substitute that season.

On 7 April 2016, Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp surprisingly started former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi ahead of Sturridge (the team's first-choice striker) during Liverpool's the Premier League quarter-final match against Borussia Dortmund, Klopp's former side. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored a vital away goal in the 1–1 draw. Three days later, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored two goals in a 4–1 win over Stoke City after coming on as a substitute to replace Sheyi Ojo at half-time.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was used predominantly as a substitute and cup player at the start of the 2016–17 campaign. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first goal of the season on 23 August 2016 in a 5–0 EFL Cup win over Burton Albion. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first 2016–17 Premier League goal on 26 November, coming off the bench for the injured Philippe Coutinho to score the opener in a 2–0 win over Sunderland.

On 31 August 2017, Bundesliga club VfL Wolfsburg announced the signing of former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi on a season-long loan deal.

On 2 December, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first goal of the season in a derby match against city rivals Everton, which Liverpool

 won 1–0. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi came on as a substitute for Roberto Firmino in the 84th minute and scored with a header in the 96th minute, capitalising on an error from Everton goalkeeper Jordan Pickford.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi has represented Belgium at under-15, under-16, under-17, under-19 and under-21 level. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored ten goals while in the under-19 team, the first in a 2013 UEFA European Under-19 Championship qualification match against Belarus on 12 October 2012.

The Football Kenya Federation expressed an interest in persuading former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi to play for the Kenya senior national team in the future. However, on 13 May 2014, Belgium senior national team manager Marc Wilmots announced former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi would be part of the 23-man squad representing Belgium at the 2014 FIFA World CupFIFA World Cup.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi came on as a substitute for Romelu Lukaku in the 58th minute of the opening Group H game against Algeria in Belo Horizonte on 17 June. In Belgium's second match, again after coming on as a substitute for Lukaku, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi first senior international goal in the 88th minute of a 1–0 win over Russia to qualify the "Red Devils" for the knockout stage. In so doing, at 19 years, 2 months and 4 days, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi became the youngest goalscorer of the tournament (until American winger Julian Green scored against Belgium during their round of 16 match), the youngest goalscorer in Belgian World Cup history, and the first player of Kenyan origin to score at a World Cup finals. For former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi performances, former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was named the Young Talent of the 2014 Belgian Sportsman of the year awards.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi scored once in Belgium's successful UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying campaign, in a 6–0 home win over Andorra on 10 October 2014. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was included in the squad for the final tournament, but missed out on the League Cup.

former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was born in Ostend and grew up in Houthalen-Oost. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi was born into a family of footballers. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi father, Mike Origi, played for KV Oostende (at the time Divock was born) and Genk, among other Belgian clubs, as well as the Kenya national team. former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi uncle, Austin Oduor, played for Gor Mahia in the Kenyan Premier League while Gor Mahia in the Kenyan Premier League other uncles, Gerald and Anthony, played for Tusker. Gor Mahia in the Kenyan Premier League cousin Arnold currently plays for Lillestrøm in the Norwegian Tippeligaen and the Kenya national team as a goalkeeper. The Origi family is of Kenyan Luo ethnicity.

On 25 June 2014, a baby dolphin at the Boudewijn Seapark in Bruges was baptised "Origi" in former Kenyan professional footballer Mike Origi honour after having scored the winning goal against Russia during Belgium's group stage match at the League Cup.
