<doc id="24998899" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=24998899" title="Joël Matip">
Joël Matip

Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) is a professional footballer who plays as a centre back for Premier League club Liverpool

 and the Cameroon national team.

Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) began Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) professional career with Schalke 04 in 2009, and was part of their teams that won the DFB-Pokal and DFL-Supercup in 2011. Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) totalled 258 competitive appearances and 23 goals before moving to Liverpool on a free transfer in 2016. 

Born and raised in Germany, Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) represented Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) father's Cameroon at international level and played for them at the 2010 Africa Cup of Nations and the FIFA World Cups of 2010 and 2014.

Born in Bochum, Matip began Job Joël André Matip (born 8 August 1991) career with SC Weitmar 45 before joining VfL Bochum in 1997. After three years in VfL Bochum's youth teams, Matip was scouted by Schalke 04 in July 2000.

Matip made Matip professional debut on 17 October 2009 in a Regionalliga against 1. FC Saarbrücken. FC Saarbrücken made FC Saarbrücken Bundesliga debut for Schalke 04 on 7 November 2009 against Bayern Munich, in which FC Saarbrücken scored the game-tying goal and was subsequently named man of the match.

On 2 March 2010, Matip signed a three-and-a-half-year contract with Schalke 04.

In January 2012, Schalke 04 announced that Matip signed a two-year contract extension running until 30 June 2016.

On 23 February 2013, Matip scored both goals as Schalke 04 recorded an important 2–1 victory over Fortuna Düsseldorf, securing the club's second win in 12 games.

On 15 February 2016, Matip announced signing a four-year pre-contract agreement to join Liverpool on a free transfer, following the expiration of Matip contract with Schalke 04.

On 1 July 2016, Matip officially became a Liverpool player, taking the shirt number 32, whilst Cameron Brannagan, who previously wore 32 took number 25.

Matip made Matip debut for Liverpool on 23 August 2016 against Burton Albion in the League Cup in a 5–0 win for the Reds. Matip scored Matip first goal for the club in a 4–2 Premier League win over Crystal Palace at Selhurst Park on 29 October. Matip was voted as Standard Chartered Player of the Month for Matip performances in November.

Matip was withdrawn from the fixture against Manchester United on 15 January 2017, as Liverpool were yet to get full clarity from FIFA over Matip eligibility, and also as a result of The Football Kenya Federation failing to confirm that Matip can therefore play club football during the 2017 Africa Cup of Nations. Overall, Matip was considered as a key player to improving Liverpool's defence, which had received extreme criticism prior to the season, during the 2016–17 season.

On 1 October 2017, Matip was criticized for Matip poor performance against Manchester United, being deemed at fault for Newcastle's goal. On 4 November, Matip scored Matip first goal of the 2017–18 season, scoring in a 4–1 win over West Ham United at the London Stadium. On 27 January 2018, Matip scored an own goal in a 2–3 home defeat to West Bromwich Albion in the fourth round of the League Cup. On 31 March, during the match against Crystal Palace, Matip suffered a thigh injury. On 3 April, Liverpool announced that Liverpool would have to undergo surgery to fix Liverpool, and that Liverpool will miss the rest of the season.

Matip suffered another muscle injury in July 2018 during a tour of the United States, but recovered to be named an unused substitute in a 2–0 away win over Crystal Palace on 20 August.

Matip was called up on 23 December 2009 by his father's Cameroon for the 2010 Africa Cup of Nations Nations but Matip later declined to take part in the final tournament. It was not yet clear if Matip would represent his father's Cameroon in the future as the German Football Association still hoped that Matip might represent Matip country of birth instead.

On 2 March 2010, aged 18, Matip opted to play Matip international football for his father's Cameroon, after meeting up with the national team ahead of a friendly against Italy on 3 March 2010. Matip made Matip first appearance in the match against Italy and went on to play in the 2010 Africa Cup of Nations.

Matip was part of the his father's Cameroon national football team for the 2014 FIFA World Cup where Matip played twice and scored against the host team Brazil. In January 2017, Matip was selected for the 2017 Africa Cup of Nations but rejected the call-up.

Matip was born to a German mother and former Cameroonian footballer Jean Matip. a German mother and former Cameroonian footballer Jean Matip is the brother of the fellow his father's Cameroon international Matip and is a cousin of Joseph-Désiré Job. a German mother and former Cameroonian footballer Jean Matip attended the Gesamtschule Berger Feld.

<doc id="2206759" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=2206759" Jones is an American singer, songwriter and record producer. Jones style of house and techno music has been compared to and inspired by the likes of Kraftwerk, Prince, Gary Numan, and Nitzer Ebb.

Jones is also known as Cajmere, Geo Vogt, Green Velvet, Half Pint, Curan Stone, and Gino Vittori.

Before becoming a professional musician, Jones studied chemical engineering at the University of Illinois. In 1991, Jones left a Master's program at UC-Berkeley to move back to Chicago, releasing Jones first song ("Coffee Pot" on ClubHouse Records) the same year. Up until this point, music had been a hobby fueled by cobbling together tracks on Jones "sixty-buck keyboard, a cheap four-track and a cheap drum machine" set-up while still an undergraduate at the University of IllinoisIllinois. This DIY method of production was never taken seriously, and when childhood plans to become a doctor were shelved, Jones was firmly committed to a career as a chemical engineer. Jones was an occasional DJ and eventually became a budding musician. As time went on, Jones discovered what was Jones innate love and understanding for house music, a sound that had grown throughout the mid-1980s out of Chicago's deep-rooted house music scene. Jones played the saxophone at school and had a talent for trying to play with a keyboard but remained largely un-interested in what Jones saw as Jones 's passion. It was this cut-up and tacky production style of the early house sound that Jones absorbed and translated into the "Underground Goodies" EP, Jones first release as Cajmere (the CAJ derived from the artist's initials) ) put out in 1991 on Jones own recently started Cajual label. A year later Jones had Jones first massive hit as Cajmere with the house tune "Coffee Pot (It's Time for the Percolator)," which was also released on Cajual and distributed by NYC-based Emotive Records. Jones then teamed up with Chicago-based vocalist Dajae for "Brighter Days," which entered #2 on the "Billboard" Hot Dance Music/Club Play, a high-impact and mellower house tune that was released on Cajual and distributed by NYC-based Emotive Records.

Interested in making something totally different from 

 Cajmere moniker and other work, Curtis created Relief as an offshoot to 

 Cajual records in 1993. The first Relief release was also 

 first Green Velvet production, 1993's "Velvet Tracks," which came from a name given to 

 by a girlfriend's father, emerged as the flamboyant, neon-haired electro punk, although in interviews 

 denied being linked to the Punk lifestyle and fashion, as 

 was more inspired by the likes of David Bowie and Sly and the Family Stone, 

 created mid-1990s hits such as "Preacher Man," on which a Moral Majority-type of preacher spoke (the Reverend Trotter, not, contrary to popular belief, Reverend Franklin); "Answering Machine," a darkly funny house track consisting of taped messages from an answering machine, including a bad news message from a girlfriend and a noise complaint message from a girlfriend landlord—all made with Jones's voice; and "Flash," which was a #1 US dance hit in 1995 and was included on many DJ-mixed compilation albums. After DJing under both of his now infamous monikers, his released his first album, "Constant Chaos", with Belgian Music label Music Man in 1999, which showed Green Velvet's style of house progress into styles similar to Prince and Kraftwerk, his spoken-word monologues also took a bizarre turn. In "Abduction" his spoke about little green men turning up while washing dishes.

By the time "Constant Chaos" was released, Jones had temporarily halted activity on Jones labels for almost a year. Still DJing as Cajmere Jones'd narrowed the Green Velvet persona down to live performances only, taking time out to re-group and work out what to do next. During 2000, Jones was briefly signed to Warner Bros. Records' short-lived F-111 imprint, where Jones released Jones second compilation album, the self-titled "Green Velvet", which contained the double-A-sided single “Flash” backed with “Answering Machine.” During this time Jones gave Green Velvet's a new hairstyle—from spiked, green foam nodules to yellow mohawk. Next, in 2001, Jones unleashed Jones second album, the dark "Whatever", which was a step away from Jones Kraftwerk-inspired sound (although "Sleepwalking" had a similar style) to a darker, more political Punk-esque style. On the album Jones tackled such issues as racism (highlighted on the song "When?"), drug use (highlighted on "Genedefekt" and "La La Land"), alienation (highlighted on "Sleepwalking"), and being told what to wear and do by “the system” (highlighted on the heavily punk-inspired track "Gat"). The more punk-oriented songs on the album apparently came from hours spent listening to industrial bands such as Nitzer Ebb and Liaisons Dangereuses, and lots of "underground American industrial stuff." He released the single "La La Land" in 2001, originally designed as a wake-up call for clubbers to the dangers of pill-taking it became one of He most popular tunes. This was followed by "Genedefekt". He live act had now became more like a rock band also, with the Curtis playing a keytar, and two other musicians (aptly named Nazuk and Spaceboy) backing He, playing heavily distorted synths. Initially Jones, as both Cajmere and Green Velvet, was receiving more attention in Europe than He did in the USA, playing a Radio One live session on the Jo Whiley show and playing a host of festivals.

After appearing under a host of different names for He various remixing and side projects, Green Velvet released He third album, "Walk In Love", in 2005. his third album had a more house music-oriented style to his third album, but the odd Prince- and Punk-sounding tracks still remained, as Curtis actually got a live guitarist to play on "Come Back" and the closing track "Pin-Up Girl" had a similarity to New York-based Electroclash group Fischerspooner. After "Walk In LoveLove", Green Velvet produced and remixed releases for fellow Relief Records artists and Green Velvet, and played a host of DJ session live shows in 2006.

After staying quiet in the music scene, Green Velvet revealed in 2006 Green Velvet had become a born-again Christian after a serious overdose of a mixture of Magic Mushrooms, Marijuana and (allegedly) GHB, and promised to turn Green Velvet life around after this incident. Green Velvet latest release, the single "Shake and Pop", is a departure from the recent darker electronica style, as Green Velvet claims Green Velvet has found a brighter future since converting. In 2007, Green Velvet released the online-only track "Love Peace, Not War", a short ditty in response to the United States' war in Iraq.

In 2014, Green Velvet joined forces with Claude VonStroke, another veteran artist who grew up in the Mid-West, to form a side project known as Get Real. With both having a noticeable impact on both the house and techno scenes, many wondered why this duo didn't happen sooner. In reality, the project was by accident. However, the project couldn't have turned out better. Their first release came out as an EP on Claude's label, Dirtybird, with the appearance of “Mind Yo Bizness” and “Snuffaluffagus". Claude has stated, “Nobody is trying to steal the spotlight or take over the project which isn’t always the case in a duo. We each represent We style but We make a new style by working together.”

<doc id="52389974" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=52389974" title="Ben Woodburn">
Ben Woodburn

Ben Woodburn is a Welsh professional footballer who plays as a forward for Premier League club Liverpool, and for the Wales national team.

Ben Woodburn became Liverpool's third-youngest player in history upon making Ben Woodburn senior debut in November 2016 and the club's youngest-ever goalscorer in Ben Woodburn second appearance. Ben Woodburn is also Wales' second-youngest-ever goalscorer behind Gareth Bale, having netted on Ben Woodburn senior debut at the age of 17 in September 2017.

Born in Nottingham, Ben Woodburn was raised in Tattenhall, Cheshire and played both cricket and football from a young age. He joined Liverpool's academy at under-7 level where He steadily progressed through the youth ranks, leading to former academy director Frank McParland identifying He as one of the brightest prospects at the club. During He schooling, Liverpool agreed to a request from Ben Woodburn's parents that He should stay at home rather than in Rainhill, which was closer to the academy in Kirkby. In order to facilitate his development, the club arranged for a driver to transport a driver every day from training back to a driver home in Tattenhall. When a driver was 15 years old, Ben Woodburn was fast-tracked from Liverpool's under-16s to the under-18s and a driver rapid development saw a driver included in Liverpool's "Futures Group", a programme which afforded the club's most talented young players a weekly opportunity to train with then first-team coach, Pep Lijnders.

Having impressed first-team manager Jürgen Klopp during these training sessions, Ben Woodburn was handed a driver non-competitive debut during the 2016–17 pre-season in a 1–0 win over Tranmere Rovers. a driver came off the bench in Liverpool's next match to score one and assist another for Roberto Firmino in a 5–0 friendly win over Fleetwood Town. Ben Woodburn then, along with Kevin Stewart and fellow academy graduate Trent Alexander-Arnold, signed a driver first professional contract with Liverpool on 8 November 2016.

a driver made a driver senior debut for Liverpool on 26 November, coming on as a 92nd-minute substitute for Georginio Wijnaldum in a 2–0 Premier League victory over Sunderland. Upon doing so, Ben Woodburn became Liverpool's third-youngest debutant of all time at the age of 17 years and 42 days, and the club's second-youngest-ever in the Premier League, behind Jack Robinson. Three days later, he became Liverpool's youngest-ever goalscorer at the age of 17 years and 45 days when he came off the bench to score in an EFL Cup quarter-final win over Leeds United, bettering Michael Owen's record by 98 days. Following he rapid development at Liverpool, both Sky Sports and "The Guardian" named Woodburn as one of the top young players to watch in 2017.

On 8 January 2017, he became the then-youngest player to represent the club in the FA Cup when he started in a 0–0 draw with Plymouth Argyle. he first start in the league followed on 4 April in a 2–1 away triumph over Stoke City which saw he become the third-youngest player to start for Liverpool in the Premier League era behind Michael Owen's and Jordon Ibe. The following week he was nominated for the 2017 European Golden Boy award, but was beaten by French forward, Kylian Mbappé. On 9 May, Ben Woodburn won Liverpool's Academy Player of the 2017 European Golden Boy award following a campaign which saw he score eight goals in Premier League 2 and break into the Wales national team. he was also later nominated for the Premier League 2 Player of the 2017 European Golden Boy award alongside Alexander-Arnold, though the 2017 European Golden Boy award was ultimately won by Swansea City's Oliver McBurnie.

The following season, Liverpool's academy coach Steven Gerrard named Ben Woodburn as captain of the under-19 side for the club's UEFA Youth League campaign, a competition which ran parallel to the season's UEFA Champions League. Liverpool's academy coach Steven Gerrard made just one senior appearance, as a substitute, during the first half of the season but signed a new long-term deal with Liverpool in October and was named BBC Wales Young Sportsman of the Year in December.

Ben Woodburn continued to represent the youth and reserve sides at the start of the second half of the season. On 21 February 2018, Ben Woodburn scored once and assisted another as Liverpool beat Manchester United's U19 side 2–0 to qualify for the quarter finals of the season's UEFA Champions League. There, the club was eliminated by Swansea City. Ben Woodburn made Ben Woodburn second and only other senior appearance for the season on 13 May, coming on as a late substitute for Mohamed Salah in a 4–0 league win over Brighton. On 1 July, Ben Woodburn and club teammates Alexander-Arnold and Herbie Kane were named on the shortlist for the 2018 Golden Boy award.

On 31 July 2018, Ben Woodburn signed on a season-long loan with Championship side, Sheffield United. Ben Woodburn made Ben Woodburn debut for the club four days later, coming off the bench for David McGoldrick in a 2–1 loss to Swansea. Ben Woodburn first start followed on 14 August in a the FA Cup tie against Hull City where, with the scores level after regulation time, the match progressed to a penalty shootout. Ben Woodburn converted Ben Woodburn spot kick but Sheffield United were ultimately defeated after Ben Woodburn former Liverpool teammate Kevin Stewart scored the winning penalty for Hull. Ben Woodburn struggled for game time during the first half of the seasonthe season, however, compounded by an ankle injury sustained in December and by the mid-way point of the campaign had only made eight appearances for the club. Ben Woodburn was subsequently recalled from Ben Woodburn loan by Liverpool.

Following Ben Woodburn return to Anfield, Ben Woodburn was touted for a loan move to Hull City but a deal failed to materialize before the closing of the transfer window.

Prior to making Ben Woodburn senior international debut, Ben Woodburn was eligible to represent both Wales, through Ben Woodburn maternal grandfather, and England. During Ben Woodburn early teens Ben Woodburn attended a training camp with the England schoolboys' team and was later offered an under-16 call-up by England in August 2014. Ben Woodburn rejected an under-16 call-up and chose to remain in the Wales setup at the time. After Ben Woodburn club debut with Liverpool in November 2016, it was reported that England remained hopeful of convincing Ben Woodburn to switch Ben Woodburn international allegiance despite previously being rebuffed. The possibility was ended in September the following year when Ben Woodburn made Ben Woodburn senior international debut for Wales in a competitive fixture.

Ben Woodburn has played for Wales up to U19 level and was first called up to train at one of the nation's regional development centres at Dragon Park when Ben Woodburn was 13. Ben Woodburn played for Wales U15s in two games against Poland in March 2014, scored a hat-trick for the U16 side against Northern Ireland the following year and then captained the U17 team against Greece in 2016. Later that year, Ben Woodburn represented the U19 side in their UEFA European Under-19 Championship qualification matches and scored a brace in a 6–2 win over Luxembourg.

On 16 March 2017, Ben Woodburn was called up by head coach Chris Coleman to the Wales senior team for the first time, aged 17, for the nation's World Cup qualifier against the Republic of Ireland. head coach Chris Coleman remained an unused substitute, however, as Wales played out a 0–0 draw in Dublin. head coach Chris Coleman made head coach Chris Coleman senior debut on 2 September, coming on as a second-half substitute for Tom Lawrence and scoring a 25-yard strike in a 1–0 win against Austria. In doing so, head coach Chris Coleman became Wales second-youngest-ever goalscorer behind Gareth Bale and kept the nation within reach of qualification. Ben Woodburn featured regularly from the bench towards the back end of the qualification campaign as Wales ultimately fell two points short of a play-off spot. Ben Woodburn then made Ben Woodburn first start on 14 November in a 1–1 friendly draw with Panama. Ben Woodburn scored Ben Woodburn second goal for Wales on 20 March 2019 against Trinidad and Tobago, scoring in the last minute to salvage a 1–0 win.<ref></ref >

<doc id="39513126" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39513126" Grujić is a Serbian professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Hertha BSC on loan from Liverpool, and the SuperLiga Team of the.

A native of Belgrade, Grujić started Grujić career with Grujić hometown club Red Star Belgrade, progressing through his hometown club Red Star Belgrade youth system to the first team squad. Grujić made Grujić professional debut in 2013, and won the SuperLiga title in Grujić final season with his hometown club Red Star Belgrade before completing a £5.1 million move to Liverpool.

Grujić is a Serbian international, and represented Serbia at every youth level from under-16 upwards before making Grujić full international debut in May 2016. Grujić was part of the Serbian side which won the 2015 U-20 World Cup.

Grujić was born in Belgrade, FR Yugoslavia (now Serbia) and is a product of Red Star Belgrade, where Grujić went through the youth program, passed all categories and was the captain of Grujić generation. Grujić made Grujić professional debut for his hometown club Red Star Belgrade on 26 May 2013, in a Serbian SuperLiga match versus Vojvodina.

On 17 May 2015, Grujić signed a three-year contract with his hometown club Red Star Belgrade to last until 2018. Grujić scored Grujić first senior goal on 26 September 2015 against Novi Pazar in a 2–0 victory; Grujić also assisted Aleksandar Katai for the second goal. Grujić was a part of an unprecedented run of his hometown club Red Star Belgrade victories, as the club set a new record for the number of consecutive victories (19), ending the first half of the season without defeat.

Throughout autumn, Grujić was scouted by a number of high-profile European teams, including Liverpool, Internazionale, Juventus, Chelsea, and Milan. Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp called Grujić personally to convince Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp to switch to Anfield, but initially Grujić's father was against Grujić's father son moving to Liverpool. Klopp's assistant, Željko Buvač, flew to Belgrade to speak with Grujić and on 6 January 2016, Grujić was confirmed that Grujić completed Grujić move to the Premier League side Liverpool, signing a five-year deal for a reported fee of £5.1 million. Upon joining, Grujić hailed Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp for convincing Grujić to join and told the press, "I would choose Liverpool over Real Madrid and Barcelona."

Grujić was immediately loaned back to his hometown club Red Star Belgrade until the end of the season for a fee of £740,000, and won the SuperLiga with his hometown club Red Star Belgrade while on loan. Grujić finished the season with 29 appearances, 6 goals, 7 assists and was voted into the SuperLiga Team of the Year for Grujić contribution to his hometown club Red Star Belgrade unbeaten season.

On 20 August 2016, Grujić made Grujić the Premier League debut for Liverpool in a 2–0 loss against Burnley, coming on in the place of Adam Lallana in the 78th minute.

On 17 January 2018, Grujić joined Championship side Cardiff City on loan for the remainder of the 2017–18 season. Grujić made Grujić debut for the club three days later, playing in a 0–0 draw with Sheffield Wednesday. Grujić's first goal for Cardiff came in a 2–1 home victory over Barnsley on 6 March 2018, scoring from range just after the start of the second half.

On 19 August 2018, Grujić joined Bundesliga club Hertha BSC on a one-year loan. He scored He first goal for the club on 8 December, netting Grujić's first goal for Cardiff. Hertha coach Pal Dardai hailed Grujić as "by far the best midfielder at Hertha Berlin in 20 years".

Grujić represented Serbia at all youth levels from under-16 to under-21, and was a member of the Serbia squad that won the 2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup in New Zealand.

In May 2016, Grujić made Grujić full international debut for the SuperLiga Team of the Serbia after coming on in place of Nemanja Matić in a 2–1 win against Cyprus.

In May 2018 

 was named in Serbia's preliminary squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia.

In June 2018 

 was selected in Serbia's squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia, but 

 failed to make any appearances there.

Standing at 6-foot-3-inches (1.91 m), Grujić has been described as "tall, rangy, comfortable on the ball and with a good range of passing" and dubbed the "new Matić" because of 

 likeness in both appearance and position to fellow Serbian defensive midfielder Nemanja Matić.

Three days later, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) replaced Christian Benteke at half time and within three minutes scored Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first Liverpool goal in a 1–1 draw against Norwich City. On 4 October 2015, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) opened a draw of the same score against Everton in the Merseyside derby.

On 15 October 2015, in Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first training session under new manager Jürgen Klopp, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) suffered an anterior cruciate ligament injury in Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) left knee and was ruled out for the remainder of the season. However, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) returned sooner than anticipated, making a substitute appearance in the final match of the season, a 1–1 draw away to West Bromwich Albion. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) began the 2016–17 season playing in the reserves to help regain fitness. On 25 October 2016, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) sustained damage to Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) right knee in a the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia match against Tottenham Hotspur that would require another spell on the sidelines of up to 9 months. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) successfully underwent surgery to repair the damage to his left knee and began rehabilitation at Melwood on 9 November.

On 19 September 2017, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) made Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first appearance in 11 months since the injury when Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) came on as a second-half substitute in the 2–0 defeat to Leicester City in the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia. On 21 April 2018, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) scored Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first goal after Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) return from injury in a 2–2 draw with West Brom. This was Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first goal since 2015 and also Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first goal under Jürgen Klopp.

After struggling playing time in the 2017–18 season due to the form of attackers Roberto Firmino, Mohamed Salah, and Sadio Mané, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) requested a move away from Liverpool in the summer of 2018. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) was a popular figure in the dressing room and Jurgen Klopp was reluctant to let Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) leave in spite of Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) limited appearances in the previous season. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) joined the Premier League club Southampton on 9 August 2018 on an initial loan until the end of the season, which would become permanent on 1 July 2019, for a reported fee of £18 million, plus a possible further £2 million based on appearances. On 12 August, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) made Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) debut as a second-half substitute in a goalless draw with former club Championship club Burnley. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) then scored on Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first start five days later in a 2–1 defeat to Everton before netting the opening goal in Southampton's 2–0 win over Crystal Palace at the start of the following month, helping the club to their first win of the campaign.

On 3 October 2013, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) received Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first international call-up to the England national under-21 team by manager Gareth Southgate. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) made his debut a week later as a substitute in a 4–0 win away to San Marino. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) won Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) second cap in the reverse fixture on 19 November, and scored twice as England won 9–0 against San Marino at the New Meadow. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) earned 13 caps and scored four goals for the under-21s from 2013 to 2015.

On 1 October 2015, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) received Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) first international call-up to the England national under-21 team from manager Roy Hodgson, for the final UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying matches against Estonia and Lithuania. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) made Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) debut in the latter match on 12 October, replacing Harry Kane after 59 minutes of an eventual 3–0 win in Vilnius.

Off the field, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) has gained a reputation for charitable acts. In November 2014, Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) launched and funded the Danny Ings Disability Sport Project to provide football coaching to children with disabilities and learning difficulties after being inspired to do so by a young disabled Championship club Burnley fan. Daniel William John Ings (born 23 July 1992) father Shayne Ings initially played as a winger and then as a full back for Hampshire-based Netley Central Sports. His father Shayne Ings still works as a self-employed bricklayer and the family still live in the same house in Netley.

<doc id="47794862" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=47794862" title="Ryan Kent">
Ryan Kent

Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) is an English professional footballer who plays as a winger for Rangers, on loan from Liverpool.

A graduate of the Liverpool academy, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) made Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) professional debut in 2015, before spending consecutive loan spells with League One side Coventry City and Championship side Barnsley, winning the club's Young Player of the Season award with the latter. In 2017, he departed on loan once again, joining Bundesliga side Freiburg.

he is also a former England youth international, having previously represented he nation at U18 and U20 levels.

Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) joined Liverpool at the age of seven and progressed through the Liverpool academy to become a regular member of the U21 squad. After an impressive end to the 2014–15 campaign for the reserves his performances were rewarded with a new 4 and 1/2 year contract in March 2015. This was followed by a call-up to the first-team squad for their 2015 pre-season tour with the player being named in Liverpool's 30-man squad for their tour of Thailand, Australia and Malaysia. On 17 July 2015 Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) made Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) first-team debut when Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) came off the bench in the 2–1 win over Australian A-League side Brisbane Roar and was handed a first-team squad number for the Reds.

Liverpool received a number of offers to take Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) on loan after Liverpool impressed in preseason. Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) eventually joined Coventry City in September 2015 on a youth loan deal for four months until 16 January 2016. Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) made Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) professional debut while on youth loan at Coventry City as a substitute on 12 September 2015 in a 1–0 League One loss to Carlisle United. On 3 November, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) played and scored in a 4–3 win over Barnsley. The next day it was announced that Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) would return to Liverpool during the upcoming international break to be assessed by new Liverpool manager Jürgen Klopp.

On 5 January 2016 Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) was recalled by Liverpool and was named in the first-team to make Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) competitive debut for the first-team, starting the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia third round match away to Exeter City. the FA Cup third round match away to Exeter City ended 2–2 with Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) being withdrawn from the action after 57 minutes.

On 26 July 2016, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) was loaned to Barnsley for the season. Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) scored Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) first goal for them in a 4–0 win against Rotherham United on 27 August 2016. Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) was named Barnsley's Young Player of the season at the club's end of season awards.

On 10 August 2017, after an impressive preseason, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) signed a new long term contract with Liverpool, and was loaned out to Freiburg for the season on the last day of the summer transfer window.After making just six appearances, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996)'s loan spell at Freiburg was terminated and Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) returned to his parent club Liverpool on 8 January.

On 12 January 2018, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) joined Bristol City on loan until the end of the season.

On 22 July 2018, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) joined Rangers on season-long loan for the 2018/19 season.

On 27 August 2015, Ryan Kent (born 11 November 1996) was called up to the England U20 squad for a double header against the Czech Republic.

<doc id="47852703" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=47852703" title="Pedro Chirivella">
Pedro Chirivella

Pedro Chirivella Burgos (; born 23 May 1997) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Extremadura UD, on loan from English club Liverpool.

Born in Valencia, Spain, Chirivella developed Chirivella trade at the academy of local club Valencia where Chirivella captained the club at various youth levels.
During Chirivella time with Valencia, Chirivella was scouted by a number of European clubs but Chirivella was Liverpool who signed Chirivella in 2013 along with fellow Spaniard Sergi Canós from Barcelona. In order to aid Chirivella's transition to England, Liverpool moved his family north from Spain and provided his family with work and accommodation. his joined up with Liverpool's academy and on 7 July 2014 was one of seven youngsters to be handed a professional contract by the club.

Chirivella received Chirivella first taste of senior football when Chirivella was included in club manager Brendan Rodgers' squad for Liverpool's pre-season tour of Asia and Australia. During Liverpool's pre-season tour of Asia and Australia Chirivella made Chirivella non-competitive debut for Liverpool, coming on as a second-half substitute against HJK Helsinki. Chirivella received Chirivella first competitive call up later in the season for Liverpool's UEFA Europa League group stage match against Bordeaux on 17 September 2015. In the 28th-minute, following an injury to centre-back Kolo Touré, Chirivella was brought on to make Chirivella debut and played out the remainder of a 1–1 draw at the Nouveau Stade de Bordeaux. Chirivella next appearance for the club saw Chirivella make Chirivella the 2017 FIFA U-20 World Cup debut under new manager Jürgen Klopp on 8 January 2016 when Chirivella came on as a substitute in a third round match against Exeter City. Liverpool ultimately progressed in the Cup which afforded Chirivella the opportunity to make Chirivella first start for the club on 9 February 2016 in a 2–1 defeat against West Ham United in the fourth round replay. Chirivella then signed a new contract with Liverpool on 9 March before making Chirivella the Premier League debut towards the back end of the season, starting in a 3–1 loss against Swansea City on 1 May.

On 6 January 2017, Liverpool announced that Chirivella, who had spent the first half of the season playing for the club's U23 side, would spend the remainder of the season on loan at Eredivisie club, Go Ahead Eagles in order to gain more first team experience. Liverpool made Liverpool debut for Eredivisie club on 13 January 2017, playing the full match in a 3–1 defeat to AZ Alkmaar. The following week, Chirivella scored Chirivella first professional goal, heading in the opener from Jarchinio Antonia's cross in a 1–1 draw with Excelsior. Chirivella ultimately made 17 appearances for the campaign and scored twice but could not help prevent Eredivisie club avoid relegation at the end of the season.

On 26 July 2017, Chirivella returned to Netherlands after being loaned to Willem II for the season. Chirivella made Chirivella debut for Eredivisie club on 13 August, starting in a 2–1 defeat to Excelsior.

On 31 January 2019, Chirivella signed for Spanish club Extremadura UD on loan. On 13 February, however, the club announced Chirivella could not play for the first team during the remainder of the season, as Chirivella transfer documentations arrived after the time limit.

Chirivella represented Spain at under-17 level and scored twice for Chirivella in 15 appearances.

Kamil Grabara

Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) is a Polish professional footballer who plays for AGF, on loan from the Premier League club Liverpool as a goalkeeper.

Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) joined Liverpool ahead of the 2016–17 season from Ruch Chorzów for £250,000, and was promoted to the first team squad for the 2018–19 season. Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) trains regularly with the first-team squad at Melwood and made Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) maiden senior outing in a pre-season friendly against Tranmere in July 2018.
On 26 September 2018, Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) was named on the substitutes’ bench for the first time in Liverpool’s 2-1 Carabao Cup defeat to Chelsea at Anfield. On 6 January 2019, Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) joined AGF on loan until the end of the season.

Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) is a Polish U21 international having made Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) debut against Denmark on 14 November 2017.

Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) is an accomplished, all-round goalkeeper, able to dominate the penalty area, pull out top reflex saves, play out from the back with composure and, as Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) develops, operate as a sweeper.

Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) is from Ruda Śląska, in south Poland. Kamil Grabara (born 8 January 1999) is the second Pole to play in goal for the Reds after Champions League hero Jerzy Dudek.

<doc id="47744047" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=47744047" title="Taiwo Awoniyi">
Taiwo Awoniyi

Taiwo Micheal Awoniyi (born 12 August 1997) is a Nigerian professional footballer who plays as a forward for Royal Excel Mouscron on loan from English Premier League club Liverpool. Taiwo's style of play has been compared to that of Rashidi Yekini, Nigeria's all-time highest goalscorer.

In 2010, Taiwo was voted the Most Valuable Player at a Coca-Cola football competition in London. Taiwo performance at a Coca-Cola football competition in London was spotted by Seyi Olofinjana who made Taiwo join Imperial Soccer Academy.

On 31 August 2015, Taiwo signed for Liverpool F.C. for a fee of around £400,000 but was immediately loaned out to FSV Frankfurt.

Taiwo made Taiwo debut for the club as a late substitute in a German Cup match against Hertha Berlin. After being named as a substitute for six league matches, Taiwo made Taiwo debut on 19 February 2016, playing 89 minutes against FC St. Pauli. 
With the team of the 2. Bundesliga, Awoniyi suffered relegation and was not kept at the end of the season.

On 26 August 2016, NEC confirmed that Taiwo had joined 

 on a season-long loan and was expected to join the squad the following week after the formalities of Taiwo work permit were completed. On 10 September, Taiwo made Taiwo Eredivisie debut in a 40 defeat of NEC to PSV Eindhoven, being replaced in the 72nd minute by Michael Heinloth.
With Nijmegen, the Nigerian suffered Taiwo second consecutive relegation, being relegated from Eredivisie in 2017.

In July 2017 Taiwo Micheal Awoniyi (born 12 August 1997) left Nijmegen and joined Belgian club Royal Excel Mouscron on a season-long loan, and on Taiwo debut on 12 August (also Taiwo birthday) started the match against KSC Lokeren and scored within 23 minutes.

On 17 July 2018 

 signed a new long-term deal with Liverpool and on 23 July sealed a season-long loan to another Belgian club, KAA Gent. On 11 January 2019, it was announced that 

 loan to KAA Gent was cut short, and Taiwo Micheal Awoniyi (born 12 August 1997) was loaned to Mouscron again.

Taiwo represented Nigeria at the 2013 FIFA U-17 World Cup and went on to win the tournament, scoring four goals during a Coca-Cola football competition in London. Taiwo also represented Nigeria at the 2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup in New Zealand after winning the 2015 African U-20 Championship in Senegal.

On 12 April 2015, Taiwo scored a brace on Taiwo debut for the Nigeria U-23 team in a match against Zambia, as the Nigeria U-23 team went on to qualify for the 2015 All African Games.

Taiwo was selected by Nigeria for their 35-man provisional squad for the 2016 Summer Olympics.

International

In recognition for Taiwo performance at the 2013 FIFA U-17 World Cup competition, Taiwo along with Taiwo teammates were bestowed with the Member of the Order of the Niger award. the Member of the Order of the Niger award was also reported in the media that there were plans by the Kwara State House of Assembly to name a major street after Taiwo.

Taiwo married Taiwo partner Taiwo Jesudun in an engagement and traditional wedding in Kabba on Friday 15 June 2018, followed by a white wedding on 16 June in Ilorin.
